Received 
      7th March 2022
    First published on 29th June 2022AbstractCovalent organic frameworks (COFs) are a class of organic crystalline porous materials discovered in the early 21st century that have become an attractive class of emerging materials due to their high crystallinity, intrinsic porosity, structural regularity, diverse functionality, design flexibility, and outstanding stability. However, many chemical and physical properties strongly depend on the presence of metal ions in materials for advanced applications, but metal-free COFs do not have these properties and are therefore excluded from such applications. Metalated COFs formed by combining COFs with metal ions, while retaining the advantages of COFs, have additional intriguing properties and applications, and have attracted considerable attention over the past decade. This review presents all aspects of metalated COFs, from synthetic strategies to various applications, in the hope of promoting the continued development of this young field.
Qun Guan
Qun Guan is currently a PhD student. He received his bachelor's degree in chemistry from the University of Jinan in 2015. He received his master's degree in organic chemistry from Shandong Normal University under the guidance of Prof. Yu-Bin Dong in 2019 and has subsequently continued his PhD studies. His research focuses on nanoscale COFs for cancer diagnosis and therapeutics.
Le-Le Zhou
Le-Le Zhou received her master's degree in organic chemistry from Shandong Normal University under the supervision of Prof. Yu-Bin Dong in 2018. Then, she worked as a lecturer at the School of Chemical and Biological Engineering, Qilu Institute of Technology, from 2018 to 2020. Currently, she is a PhD student under the supervision of Prof. Yu-Bin Dong. Her research interests are advanced materials for preventing and treating tumors.
Yu-Bin Dong
Prof. Dr Yu-Bin Dong is the Chang Jiang Scholar of chemistry at Shandong Normal University. He obtained his PhD from Nankai University (under Prof. Li-Cheng Song) in 1996. He then joined Prof. Andreas Mayr's group at The University of Hong Kong and Prof. Hans-Conrad zur Loye's group at the University of South Carolina from 1996 to 2000, and was promoted to full professor at Shandong Normal University in 2000. He is the author of over 200 peer-reviewed publications. His current research interests are mainly focused on MOF and COF materials and their applications in catalysis, sensing, bioimaging, and cancer treatment.
1. Introduction
Covalent organic frameworks (COFs) are covalent bond-linked two-dimensional (2D) or three-dimensional (3D) organic crystalline frameworks constructed from organic monomers composed entirely of light elements (e.g., C, N, O, B, and S).1–4 According to the groundbreaking work by Yaghi et al. in 2005, the first reported COFs, i.e., COF-1 and COF-5, were respectively prepared by self-condensation of 1,4-phenylenediboronic acid and co-condensation of 1,4-phenylenediboronic acid with triphenylene-2,3,6,7,10,11-hexaol under solvothermal conditions (Fig. 1A).5 As shown, the boroxine-linked COF-1 features a 2D structure with staggered AB stacking mode, whereas the boronate ester-linked 2D COF-5 adopts an eclipsed AA stacking structure. Since then, COFs with different linkages and topologies have been synthesized one after another by various approaches including solvothermal,6–9 ionothermal,10,11 microwave,12,13 atmospheric solution,14–18 mechanochemical,19–21 electrochemical,22,23 photochemical,24,25 and other methods.26–29 The CURATED-COFs database30 established by Smit et al. has included 648 COFs as of June 2021. The variety of COFs has been still increasing rapidly since the release of this archive to date. A search of the Scopus (Elsevier B.V.) database on May 2, 2022 showed that the query string TITLE-ABS-KEY (“Covalent Organic Framework”) retrieved over 4300 research papers and close to 1000 patents, covering various subject areas such as chemistry, materials science, chemical engineering, and environmental science.31
 Fig. 1  Basic concepts of COFs. (A) Schematic diagram of the formation of COF-1 and COF-5. (B) Timeline of COFs with representative covalent linkages reported so far. (C) Reported topologies of 2D COFs. 
The diverse linkage chemistry of COFs is the basis not only for investigating the structure–property relationship, but also for expanding the applications of COFs (Fig. 1B). Early studies focused on the COFs linked by dynamic covalent bonds. The reversibility of the linkages allows self-correction of defects formed during the reaction, resulting in COFs with ordered structures and thermodynamic stability. For example, the reversibility of the B–O bonds was essential for crystallinity of boronate ester-linked 3D COF-102 reported by Yaghi et al. in 2007.32 COFs linked by reversible imine bonds were first reported in 2009,33 which are one of the most reported subclasses of COFs to date due to the diversity of aromatic amine and aldehyde monomers. However, to some extent, the reversibility of the bonds reduces the chemical stability of the framework. To date, several irreversible linkages have been developed to synthesize COFs. For example, β-ketoenamine-linked COFs with high chemical stability can be synthesized by combining reversible Schiff base reactions and irreversible tautomerism reactions.34 Furthermore, when the ortho position of an aromatic amine is occupied by a nucleophilic group (e.g., –OH, –NH2, and –SH), the cascade reaction of imine condensation–oxidative cyclization can be used to obtain benzoxazole-, benzoimidazole-, and benzothiazole-linked COFs.35–37 Dioxin-linked COFs can be obtained by irreversible nucleophilic substitution reactions of fluorobenzenes and phenols.38 In 2022, pyridinium-linked COF films were synthesized via the irreversible Katritzky reaction of pyrylium and arylamines.39 Moreover, multicomponent reactions were used in the construction of chemically robust COFs. The three-component Strecker reaction, aza-Diels–Alder reaction, Debus–Radziszewski reaction, sulfur cyclization reaction, Groebke–Blackburn–Bienaymé reaction, A3-coupling reaction, and Kabachnik–Fields reaction have been used for COF synthesis with α-aminonitrile,40 quinoline,40 benzimidazole,41 benzothiazole,42 imidazo[1,2-a]pyridine,43 propargylamine44 and α-aminophosphonate45 linkages, respectively. In addition, the construction of COFs linked by amine,46,47 amide48,49 benzothiazole,50 and azo51 moieties based on post-synthetic modification of imine-linked COFs greatly enriched the variety of COFs.
In addition to linkages, the topology of COFs is also an important source of structural diversity of COFs (Fig. 1C). Based on the design strategy of modular condensation polymerization, at least 9 kinds of topologies of 2D monolayers, i.e., hcb,5,52sql,53,54kgm,55–58cem,59hxl,60cpi,61bex,62,63kgd,64–66 and tth,63,66 have been reported by combining more than one organic monomer or making the pore structure dissymmetric via changing the edge lengths and vertex angles.67 Moreover, the 2D monolayers may adopt different stacking modes in space, e.g., AA,5 AB,5,68,69 and ABC,70–74 further enriching the structural diversity of 2D COFs. Conversely, less than 100 different 3D COFs have been reported since the first report in 2007.32 The variety of reported 3D COFs is significantly less than that of 2D COFs largely due to their complicated structural determination and the limited availability of organic monomers that form highly connected 3D reticulations.75,76 However, 3D COFs have an abundant changeable topology.77 3D COFs with ctn,32,78bor,32dia,33,79rra,80pts,81–85lon,86ljh,87 and nbo88 topologies have been formed based on four-connected monomers with tetrahedral Td symmetry. Six-connected monomers with trigonal prism D3h symmetry led to stp,89ceq,90acs,91–93 and hea94 topologies, while D3d- and C3-symmetric six-connected monomers have been implemented in the synthesis of 3D COFs with pcu95 and soc96 topologies, respectively. Eight-connected building monomers produced 3D COFs with bcu97 and pcb98 topologies. Furthermore, by introducing specific geometric constraints into the monomers to control the spatial orientation of reactive groups in the monomers, the topological types of 3D COFs were further enriched, including ffc,99fjh,100 and tbo101 topologies formed by [4+3] condensation reactions and srs102 topology formed by [3+3] condensation reactions.
As crystalline porous materials, COFs have the advantages of modularity, crystallinity, porosity, and versatility.103–106 Generally, COFs are chemically stable in water and organic solvents as well as under acidic, alkaline, and oxidizing conditions. These features enable the use of COFs as functional materials for various applications under different conditions, including for adsorption and separation,107–111 catalysis,112–115 nanomedicine,116–120 sensing,121–124 photochemistry,125 electrochemistry,126 energy storage,127 and many others.
However, since COFs are metal-free, they cannot meet the requirement of applications that require the presence of metals. Recent studies revealed that COFs with potential coordination sites can act as supramolecular ligands and carriers to bind and stabilize metal ions or metal-containing nanoparticles, further enhancing the functionality of COF-based materials.128 Since metal species are not involved in the construction of the COF-backbones, the metalation does not generally affect their crystallinity and structural features, providing unparalleled flexibility for combining the advantages of COF and metal species.
Since the impressive example of a Pd(II)-coordinated COF reported in 2011,129 metalated COFs have undergone more than a decade of rapid development, particularly in the last 5 years, and numerous metalated COFs have been reported to date (Table 1).129–151 The metalated COFs display various properties that cover almost all possible application fields. Metalated COFs are being increasingly recognized as a new class of organic–inorganic hybrid materials.152,153 However, surveys of achievements related to metalated COFs are scattered in various review articles,67,77,154–176 and no comprehensive and complete review articles dedicated only to metalated COFs are currently available in the literature,128,177 hampering the further development of this promising and rapidly evolving field.

In this review, we provide an exhaustive and systematic overview and discussion of the metalated COFs that have been realized to date, including their synthetic strategies and cutting-edge applications in the past decade. Furthermore, the remaining challenges and personal perspectives on the further development of metalated COFs are presented. We are convinced that this timely review not only will inspire the researchers in the COF-field and the interdisciplinary areas of chemistry, materials science, but it can also be highly beneficial for the future design and development of functionalized COFs.
2. Synthetic strategy of metalated COFs
The methods for the introduction of metal ions into COFs through coordination, known as metalation,178 include both pre-synthetic and post-synthetic routes.179 In pre-synthetic metalation, the complexes are used directly as the monomers for the construction of COFs, and the amount and position of the metals in the COFs can be precisely controlled. However, the solubility and reactivity of the metalated monomers may be different from those of the metal-free monomers, so that the synthesis conditions of COFs must be optimized iteratively. In addition, for the complexes that are unstable under violent reaction conditions (e.g., solvothermal synthesis), it is difficult to avoid the leaching of metal ions. Fortunately, post-synthetic metalation provides an effective alternative approach for the synthesis of metal-modified COFs. Through either direct coordination or ligand exchange, metal ions can be anchored to COF-frameworks while maintaining the original crystallinity of COFs, and their contents can be regulated by simply changing the concentration and reaction time in the reaction system. During this process, the regularly arranged non-metal atoms in COFs act as a well-defined net that becomes a reticular chemical ligand for accurate capture of metal ions. Furthermore, since metal ions are not vital for the support of the COF-backbone, more than one metal can be easily embedded in the COFs as required and their content and ratio can be readily adjusted without affecting the crystallinity, providing unparalleled flexibility for combining the advantages of the COFs and the metals.
Depending on the position of the metal ions in the metalated COFs, metalated COFs can be divided into three categories: (i) metal ions are coordinated to the COF monomeric units; (ii) metal ions are coordinated to the linkages of the COFs; and (iii) metal ions are embedded in the COFs as nanoparticles. In this section, we will introduce these three types of metalated COFs, with a special focus on their structural and synthetic chemistry.
2.1. Metal–monomer coordination

2.1.1. Porphyrin. 
Porphyrins are a representative class of macrocyclic heterocyclic compounds formed by connecting the α-carbon atoms of four pyrrole subunits linked by methines (CH–).180 Due to their planar structure and easy functionalization, porphyrins have been widely used as monomers for the construction of COFs containing π-conjugated systems.181
Most of the reported porphyrin-COFs are based on porphyrins with C4 symmetry, such as 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)-21H,23H-porphyrin and 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-formylphenyl)-21H,23H-porphyrin. Regarding topology, the [4+2] combination of square and linear monomers yielded a 2D sql network. In 2011, Yaghi et al. reported a typical 2D porphyrin-COF, COF-366, that was synthesized by the condensation of 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)-21H,23H-porphyrin and terephthalaldehyde.182 Later, Jiang et al. synthesized the DhaTph COF using 2,5-dihydroxyterephthalaldehyde rather than terephthalaldehyde in o-dichlorobenzene and ethanol solvents.183 Because the in-frame hydrogen bonds protect the imine from hydrolysis under acidic conditions, the DhaTph COF is chemically more stable than COF-366. In addition, the [4+4] combination of two square-planar molecules can also form a 2D sql network. As an example, COF-420 was synthesized by imine condensation between two porphyrin monomers, namely 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)-21H,23H-porphyrin and 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-formylphenyl)-21H,23H-porphyrin.184,185 Similarly, H2P-TPE-COF186 and TTCOF-2H187 were synthesized by the [4+4] strategy based on porphyrins and rhombic monomers. Furthermore, the combination of planar porphyrins with tetrahedral molecules can provide 3D COFs. In 2017, Wang et al. reported the first 3D porphyrin-COF with pts topology through the [4+4] imine condensation of 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-formylphenyl)-21H,23H-porphyrin and tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)methane.188 In addition to C4 symmetry, porphyrins with C2 symmetry were also employed for the construction of COFs. For example, in 2013, Echegoyen et al. reported the CoPc-PorDBA COF with the sql topology in the P4/mmm space group based on the 5,15-bis(4-dioxylborylphenyl)porphyrin building block.189 One year later, Bein et al. obtained the TP-Por COF with the hcb topology by the [3+2] co-condensation of 2,3,6,7,10,11-hexahydroxytriphenylene and 5,15-bis(4-boronophenyl)porphyrin.190
An important structural advantage of porphyrins is that they have four pyrrolic nitrogen atoms arranged in squares that serve as effective chelating sites to trap metal ions, providing abundant possibilities for COF metalation (Fig. 2).
 Fig. 2  Pre- and post-synthetic metalation of porphyrin-based COF-366. 
Metalated porphyrins (viz. metalloporphyrins) are used directly as monomers for the synthesis of COFs; this is referred to as pre-synthetic metalation. In 2013, Jiang and co-workers reported that the CuP-Ph COF was obtained by the reaction of copper 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin with terephthalaldehyde under solvothermal conditions.191 The replacement of half terephthalaldehyde with 2,3,5,6-tetrafluoroterephthalaldehyde significantly increased the crystallinity of COFs, and the Brunauer–Emmett–Teller (BET) specific surface area increased from 926 to 1389 m2 g−1, which is attributed to the self-complementary electronic interactions in the COFs. In the same year, the same group reported an additional squaraine-linked porphyrin-COF, namely, CuP-SQ, by the solvothermal reaction (o-dichlorobenzene/n-butanol, 85 °C, 7 days) of copper 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin with squaric acid in a high yield of 94%.192 Due to the π-conjugated linkage together with the eclipsed stacking mode, this COF possesses enhanced chemical and thermal stability.
Furthermore, 2D metalloporphyrin-COFs may be a diversified resource library for the development of ultrathin nanosheets and membranes with potentially enhanced functional performances due to the high accessibility of exposed metal sites on the surface. Very recently, Feng et al. employed the irreversible Katritzky reaction of zinc 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin with 4,4′-(1,4-phenylene)bis(2,6-diphenylpyrylium) tetrafluoroborate to prepare the pyridinium-linked C2DP-ZnPor COF films on the water surface.39 The obtained C2DP-ZnPor COF has a large crystal size of 30–80 μm2 and a thickness of approximately 25 nm. A square lattice with a cell parameter of 30.5 Å can be clearly observed by high resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM). In addition to copper(II)101,145,188,193 and zinc(II) porphyrin,130,194,195 other metalloporphyrins such as cobalt(II),195–197 palladium(II),198 nickel(II),135,193,199,200 manganese(II),201 and iron(III) porphyrins202 can also tolerate the solvothermal conditions, and can be directly embedded into COFs by similar reactions, achieving the corresponding metalated COFs with unique properties that are not available in the metalloporphyrin monomers.
In addition to homometallic porphyrin-COFs, the construction of heterometallic porphyrin-COFs is also feasible through the use of mixed metalloporphyrin monomers. In 2019, Feng et al. reported heterometallic porphyrin-COFs that were prepared from tetraamino- and tetraformaldehyde-substituted porphyrins with different metal ions via the [4+4] imine condensation reactions.185 By adjusting the central metals in the metalloporphyrins, Por-COF-ZnCu and Por-COF-ZnNi can be obtained, enabling laser-induced nonlinear optical applications. Additionally, the metal content in the heterometallic COFs is adjustable due to the flexibility of the raw material ratios. For instance, Chang and co-workers employed the reaction of 4,4′-diformylbiphenyl with different ratios of cobalt 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin and copper 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin for the synthesis of COF-367-Co/Cu to achieve the controlled electrochemical and spectroelectrochemical properties.134
Besides direct polymerization of the metalloporphyrin monomers, post-synthetic modification is an additional powerful approach for COF metalation. For example, by refluxing metal-free 3D porphyrin-COF (PCOF-1) with ferrous chloride in N,N-dimethylformamide (DMF), the Fe-metalated PCOF-1-Fe COF was obtained, which was reported by Gu et al. in 2019.203 In addition, the authors prepared the cobalt-doped PCOF-1-Co in a similar way. The resulting PCOF-Fe exhibited considerable biocatalytic activity, and PCOF-Co had good electrocatalytic activity of oxygen evolution. Interestingly, the post-synthetic metalation of porphyrin-COFs sometimes can promote the exfoliation of bulk COFs. As shown in the recent reports by Osakada et al. in 2019204 and 2022,205 when the metal-free TphDha COF was refluxed with metal salts (e.g., Mg(ClO4)2 and CuSO4) in pyridine, the bulk TphDha COF was exfoliated into 2D nanosheets with a thickness of less than 3 nm due to the formation of metalloporphyrin and axial coordination of pyridine. When 4-methylpyridine and 4-ethylpyridine that are larger molecules than pyridine were used as the axial ligands, nanosheets with a thickness of only 1 nm were obtained. In conclusion, post-synthetic metalation circumvents the shortcomings of metalloporphyrin monomers in terms of stability and solubility.


2.1.2. Phthalocyanine. 
Phthalocyanine, as a derivative of tetraazaporphyrin, is a conjugated macrocyclic compound with 18π electrons that is composed of four isoindole rings connected by nitrogen atoms.206 The cavity with a diameter of approximately 2.7 Å in the center of the phthalocyanine ring can bind metal ions such as Cu(II), Zn(II), and Co(II) through four coordinate bonds to form highly stable metallophthalocyanines. Since their accidental synthesis in the early 20th century, metallophthalocyanines have been widely used in the dye industry and as photoelectric functional materials.207 To date, only octahydroxyphthalocyanine, hexadecafluorophthalocyanine, octaaminophthalocyanine and octacarboxyphthalocyanine tetraanhydrides have been used as monomers for the synthesis of metallophthalocyanine-COFs. The synthesis involved 6 types of condensation reactions and only three kinds of topological structures (Fig. 3).
 Fig. 3  Metallophthalocyanine-based COFs. (A) Structures of metallophthalocyanine building blocks. (B) Schematic illustration of the metallophthalocyanine-involved condensation reactions. (C) Schematic diagram of sql, nbo, and pts topological structures. 
The first synthesis of phthalocyanine-COFs from 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanines (or the corresponding acetonides) and linear diboronic acids was reported by the Dichtel group in 2010,208 while the corresponding metallophthalocyanine analogs (i.e., metallophthalocyanine-COFs) were reported by the same group in 2012.131 By varying the length of the diboronic acid monomers, the zinc(II) phthalocyanine-COFs with pore size in the range of 2.7–4.4 nm were obtained (Fig. 4). In addition to zinc(II) phthalocyanine, copper(II),209 nickel(II),209,210 and cobalt(II) phthalocyanine189,211 can also serve as metallomonomers for creating borate-linked COFs, which was demonstrated by Jiang and Echegoyen groups independently. For example, the reaction of copper(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine with N,N′-di(4-boronophenyl)perylene-3,4,9,10-tetracarboxylic diimide led to DCuPc–APDI-COF, whereas the combination of nickel(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine with N,N′-di(4-boronophenyl)benzene-1,2,4,5-tetracarboxylic diimide and N,N′-di(4-boronophenyl)naphthalene-1,4,5,8-tetracarboxylic diimide resulted in DNiPc–APyrDI-COF and DNiPc–ANDI-COF, respectively.209 These metalated donor–acceptor COFs have long charge separation lifetimes, whereas the photochemical dynamics properties are closely related to the embedded metal species, the acceptor species, and the local geometry between the donor and acceptor units. Furthermore, the CoPc-BPDA COF, a cobalt(II) phthalocyanine-COF, was prepared by the solvothermal reaction of cobalt(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine with [1,1′-biphenyl]-4,4′-diyldiboronic acid, and it possesses moderate H2 (1.2 wt% at 77 K/1.0 bar) and CH4 (0.59 wt% at 273 K/1.0 bar) uptakes.211
 Fig. 4  Octahydroxyphthalocyanines for constructing borate-, spiroborate- and dioxin-linked COFs. 
An impressive Co(II)-metalated phthalocyanine-COF, namely SPB-COF-DBA,88 with nbo topology was reported by Cooper et al. in 2021 (Fig. 4). It was prepared by the reaction of cobalt(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine with trimethyl borate at 120 °C in N,N-dibutylformamide under self-generated pressure. In its framework, the adjacent cobalt(II) phthalocyanine species are located in two perpendicular planes and connected by the negatively charged spiroborate linkage, while the in situ generated dibutylammonium from N,N-dibutylformamide decomposition under the given conditions acts as the charge-balancing cation. Structural analysis by powder X-ray diffraction (PXRD) showed that SPB-COF-DBA crystallizes in a cubic symmetric structure with the cell parameter a = 34.744 Å and the Imm space group. In addition, the solid state nuclear magnetic resonance (ssNMR) signal of 11B is located at 14.0 ppm and the B–O stretching vibrations in the Fourier transform infrared (FT-IR) spectrum are located between 1026 and 1053 cm−1, indicating the formation of spiroborate. Interestingly, the counter ions in SPB-COF-DBA can be adjusted by changing the solvent systems. For example, the solvents dimethylamine and 1-methylpyrrolidin-2-one led to dimethylammonium, whereas the tetrabutylammonium hydroxide medium resulted in tetrabutylammonium as the counter cation. Although SPB-COF-DBA is more stable than some reported borate-linked COFs, it still cannot tolerate 1 M HCl due to the intrinsic susceptibility of the spiroborate linkage to acidic media.
For achieving chemically more stable COFs, the dioxin-linked metallophthalocyanine-COFs have been recently designed and synthesized (Fig. 4). In the late 2020, Lan and co-workers reported a series of NiPc–TFPN, CoPc–TFPN, and ZnPc–TFPN COFs based on irreversible aromatic nucleophilic substitution reactions between 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxymetallophthalocyanines and 2,3,5,6-tetrafluoroterephthalonitrile under solvothermal conditions (N,N-dimethylacetamide/mesitylene, triethylamine, 150 °C).212 These dioxin-linked COFs display high crystallinity and exceptional stability. Thermogravimetric analysis showed that the NiPc–TFPN COF is thermally stable up to 400 °C in nitrogen and up to 300 °C in oxygen. In addition, these COFs were able to withstand extreme environments, such as concentrated acids and bases, for at least 1 month without obvious loss of crystallinity. Furthermore, as shown by Zhang et al.,213 the CoPc–TFPN COF can maintain its crystallinity even in 30% H2O2 and 1 M NaBH4, with a weight loss of less than 10%. In 2021, heterometallic dioxin-linked COFs were synthesized by Huang et al. by the combination of cobalt(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine and copper(II) 1,2,3,4,8,9,10,11,15,16,17,18,22,23,24,25-hexadecafluorophthalocyanine under solvothermal conditions.147 The obtained CuPcF8–CoPc-COF and CuPcF8–CoNPc-COF are chemically stable under harsh conditions. Moreover, their pseudo-AA stacking mode of metallophthalocyanine species enables a high-speed electron transfer pathway, resulting in that both metalated COFs exhibit satisfactory activity and selectivity toward electrocatalytic CO2 reduction in an aqueous solution. Of note, around 10% Cu(II) in CuPcF8–CoPc-COF was reduced to Cu(I) due to the reducibility of DMF and triethylamine. Follow-up studies have shown that the reaction at 180 °C with K2CO3 can effectively prevent Cu(II) reduction.214
Metalated octaaminophthalocyanines have recently been developed for the synthesis of pyrazine-linked COFs. In 2019, Mirica et al. reported COF-DC-8,215 which was obtained by the reaction of 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octaaminophthalocyaninato nickel(II) and pyrene-4,5,9,10-tetraone in the solvent system of N,N-dimethylacetamide and o-dichlorobenzene with sulfuric acid under solvothermal conditions (202 °C, 10 days). Interestingly, microwave heating significantly shortened the reaction time to 10 h. In 2020, Jiang et al. synthesized CoPc-PDQ-COF, a Co-based analogue of COF-DC-8, in a mixture of ethylene glycol and N,N-dimethylacetamide with the aid of acetic acid at 200 °C for 7 days.216 CoPc-PDQ-COF, as a phenazine-linked stable and conductive COF, can be an ideal electrocatalyst for CO2 reduction to CO in aqueous media. Interestingly, a steric effect is present in pyrazine-linked phthalocyanine-COFs. By introducing bulky substituents (e.g., tert-butyl), COF layer stacking deviates from the classical AA mode, leading to slip stacking, which was recently observed by Feng et al.217 MPc-pz COFs (M = Zn, Cu) were synthesized by the condensation reaction of 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octaaminophthalocyaninato zinc(II)/cooper(II) with 2,7-di-tert-butylpyrene-4,5,9,10-tetraone in 1-methyl-2-pyrrolidone/mesitylene (150 °C, 3 days) with p-toluenesulfonic acid (Fig. 5). The PXRD analysis combined with first-principles calculations showed that both COFs are consistent with a serrated AA stacking which was caused by the tert-butyl groups in pyrazine moieties. Subsequently, MPc-pz COFs (M = Fe, Co, Ni, Mn, Zn, Cu) were also prepared by the same group but using more soluble (diphenylmethylene)amino-substituted metallophthalocyanines as precursors. During the synthesis, 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octaaminometallophthalocyanines were in situ generated, thereby lowering the polymerization rates and providing pyrazine-linked COFs with superior crystallinity and high average crystal size.148 Recently, Cao et al. reported a nickel(II)-containing pyrazine-linked COF. As an isomorphic analogue of MPc-pz COFs, it also possesses a 2D layered structure with serrated AA stacking.218
 Fig. 5  Pyrazine-linked phthalocyanine-based 2D COFs. (A) Synthesis of MPc-pz COFs (M = Zn, Cu). Reaction condition: p-toluenesulfonic acid, 1-methyl-2-pyrrolidone, mesitylene, 150 °C, 3 days. (B) Serrated AA stacking of MPc-pz COFs (M = Zn, Cu). 
In addition to the pyrazine-linked COFs, the piperazine-linked phthalocyanine-COF has also been reported by Huang and co-workers. By Buchwald–Hartwig cross-coupling reaction of nickel(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octaaminophthalocyanine and cobalt(II) 1,2,3,4,8,9,10,11,15,16,17,18,22,23,24,25-hexadecafluorophthalocyanine under solvothermal conditions (dioxane, triethylamine, 120 °C), the piperazine-linked heterometallic NiPc–NH–CoPcF8 COF was generated.219 NiPc–NH–CoPcF8 crystallized in the tetragonal P4/mmm space group, with AA stacking mode, a pore size of 1.1 nm, and an interlayer spacing of 3.6 Å. Not surprisingly, NiPc–NH–CoPcF8 is chemically stable toward water, common organic solvents, 6 M NaOH, and 6 M HCl.
In addition, the imide-linked metalated phthalocyanine-COFs also appeared in the recent literature.220 In 2021, Jiang and co-workers employed cobalt(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octacarboxyphthalocyanine tetraanhydrides to react with benzene-1,4-diamine in the binary solvent of N-methylpyrrolidone and n-butanol under the catalysis of isoquinoline at 180 °C for 5 days to synthesize imide-linked COFs. The obtained CoPc–PI-COF-1 was indexed to the eclipsed AA-stacking structure in the P4/mmm space group with the cell parameters a = b = 21.02 Å and c = 3.34 Å. Moreover, attempts to replace benzene-1,4-diamine with benzidine resulted in CoPc–PI-COF-2 with a similar structure to that of CoPc–PI-COF-1. In the same year, Jiang and co-workers used the same cobalt(II) phthalocyanine monomer but with 4,4′,4′′,4′′′-(adamantane-1,3,5,7-tetrayl)tetraaniline with the Td molecular symmetry to get a Co-metalated phthalocyanine-based 3D COF.85 The generated CoPc–PI-COF-3 has a three-fold interpenetrated pts topology with the cell parameters a = b = 24.6 Å, c = 44.4 Å, α = β = γ = 90°. The evaluation of chemical stability showed that CoPc–PI-COF-1, CoPc–PI-COF-2, and CoPc–PI-COF-3 are stable in 12 M HCl, 0.5 M KHCO3 and various organic solvents for at least 20 days.
In addition to the direct polymerization of metallophthalocyanine monomers, the metallophthalocyanine-COFs can also be synthesized from the in situ polymerization of the phthalocyanine precursors with metal templates. In 2019, Xiang et al. employed the one-pot in situ reaction of benzene-1,2,4,5-tetracarbonitrile and FeCl3 or CuCl2 with the 1,8-diazabicyclo[5.4.0]undec-7-ene (DBU) catalyst under either microwave heating (180 °C, 15 min) or solvothermal conditions (180 °C, 3 days) to generate a fully closed conjugated planar COFBTC.221 Notably, the addition of 3,6-dihydroxyphthalonitrile to the reaction system could decrease the condensation reaction rate, consequently, controlling the particle size of the phthalocyanine-COFs.222 Compared with the COFs directly obtained from phthalocyanine monomers, the metallophthalocyanine-COFs synthesized by this method have better aqueous dispersibility but worse crystallinity.
Of note, the metallophthalocyanine-COFs with 5th and 6th period metals (e.g., Pt, Rh, Ag, W, Ta, Mo, Os, and Re) have been predicted based on first-principles density functional theory calculations,223 but their synthesis still remains blank.


2.1.3. Naphthalocyanine. 
Naphthalocyanine is an analog of phthalocyanine that can be regarded as tetrabenzophthalocyanine. In 2021, Huang et al. first synthesized naphthalocyanine-COFs, including NiPcF8–NiNPc-COF, CoPcF8–CoNPc-COF, CuPcF8–CuNPc-COF, and CuPcF8–CoNPc-COF, using the solvothermal reaction of 3,4,12,13,21,22,30,31-octahydroxylnaphthalocyanines with 1,2,3,4,8,9,10,11,15,16,17,18,22,23,24,25-hexadecafluorophthalocyanines under alkaline conditions (Fig. 6).147 All of these naphthalocyanine-COFs are linked by a dioxin linkage and have the AA stacking mode, exhibiting strong stability under harsh conditions.
 Fig. 6  Synthesis of metallonaphthalocyanine-based COFs via organic base-catalytic aromatic nucleophilic substitution reactions. 


2.1.4. 2,2′-Bipyridine. 
As one of the most common classes of bidentate N,N′-type ligands, 2,2′-bipyridines, which are easily functionalized at the 5,5′-positions, are ideal candidates for the synthesis of metalated COFs (Fig. 7).
 Fig. 7  Post-synthetic metalation of the TpBpy COF via coordination reaction of the metal ion and ligand exchange reaction of the coordination compound. 
The solvothermal synthesis of metallobipyridine-COFs using 2,2′-bipyridine complexes is sometimes limited by their chemical stability. As revealed by Banerjee et al. in 2017, the solvothermal reaction (N,N-dimethylacetamide/1,4-dioxane, HOAc, 90 °C, 3 days) of (5,5′-diamino-2,2′-bipyridine)dichloropalladium(II) with 2,4,6-trihydroxybenzene-1,3,5-tricarbaldehyde caused the Pd(II) reduction during the COF formation, and Pd nanoparticle-loaded Pd@TpBpy was obtained.224 However, the mechanochemical synthesis can circumvent this issue, but the obtained Pd(II)-metalated Pd-TpBpy COF has poor crystallinity.225 In addition, the room temperature synthesis of COFs is also a feasible approach,226 but may not meet the high crystallinity requirements of most COFs. The attempt to synthesize Re(I)-chelated 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs, however, was successful.227 Marinescu and co-workers revealed that the reaction of tricarbonylchloro(5,5′-dicarbaldehyde-2,2′-bipyridine)rhenium(I) and 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin in o-dichlorobenzene/n-butanol at 120 °C for 2 days could successfully give Re-BpyPor-COF, which may be attributed to the acceptable chemical stability of the rhenium complex under the given conditions. In addition, attempts for direct synthesis of the Co(II)-coordinated 2,2′-bipyridine-COF on the surface of CdS nanowires have also been successfully achieved by Wang et al. recently.228
By comparison, post-synthetic metalation of 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs is a scalable method. On the one hand, metal ion-coordinated 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs can be directly obtained by reacting metal-free 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs with the corresponding metal salts. As reported by the Kurungot group in 2016,136 Co(II)-metalation of the imine-linked TpBpy COF that was formed from 2,4,6-trihydroxybenzene-1,3,5-tricarbaldehyde and [2,2′-bipyridine]-5,5′-diamine can be easily realized in a Co(CH3COO)2 methanol solution via the 2,2′-bipyridine-cobalt(II) coordination. In the solid ultraviolet-visible diffuse reflectance spectrum (UV-vis DRS) of the cobalt(II)-chelated Co-TpBpy COF, new strong absorption bands appear at 470 and 510 nm, corresponding to the charge-transfer transition. Similarly, other metal ions, such as Fe(III),229 Cu(II),230–232 Ag(I),233 and rare earth ions,146 can also be introduced into 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs by the same post-synthetic metalation approach. In addition, when two metal salts are used, the heterobimetallic 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs can be easily obtained, which was well demonstrated by Sun et al.234 On the other hand, the ligand exchange between 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs and metal-complexes is an additional feasible approach for the preparation of metalated 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs. As shown by Huang and co-workers in 2018,141 by the reaction of the established TTA-BPDA-COF—which was generated from 4,4′,4′′-(1,3,5-triazine-2,4,6-triyl)trianiline and [2,2′-bipyridine]-5,5′-dicarbaldehyde—with Re(CO)5Cl under reflux in toluene, the two coordinated CO ligands were exchanged by the 2,2′-bipyridine moieties on TTA-BPDA-COF, thus anchoring Re(I) as Re(2,2′-bipyridine)(CO)3Cl on the pore walls of the COF. As shown, the existence of the Re(2,2′-bipyridine)(CO)3Cl structural unit was supported by X-ray absorption and ssNMR spectra. Briefly, post-synthetic metalation is a general and versatile method for 2,2′-bipyridine-COF metalation that has been widely used for the synthesis of metalated 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs, as summarized in Table 2.136,141,146,229–254

Different from the metalloporphyrin- and metallophthalocyanine-COFs, the metalated 2,2′-bipyridine-COFs might possess higher activity due to their often existent coordinatively unsaturated metal centers. However, the free rotation of the pyridine rings in 2,2′-bipyridine monomers could sometimes lead to weak coordination interactions between metal ions and N donors, which would cause the metal ions to leach from COF-scaffolds. This has a negative impact on the stability of metallo-2,2′-bipyridine-COFs, consequently, limiting their application, especially in catalysis under relatively harsh conditions.


2.1.5. 1,10-Phenanthroline. 
1,10-Phenanthroline is a 2,2′-bipyridine analog but with rotationally restricted pyridine rings. It is found that 1,10-phenanthroline monomers can coordinate with metal ions in the form of V-shaped 2,9-disubstituted- or linear 3,8-disubstituted-1,10-phenanthrolines.
In 2016, Yaghi et al. reported COF-505-Cu as the first example of woven COFs via the reaction of the V-shaped 2,9-disubstituted-1,10-phenanthroline tetrahedral complexes with a linear monomer (Fig. 8A).137 The Cu(PDB)2BF4 monomer from 4,4′-(1,10-phenanthroline-2,9-diyl)dibenzaldehyde (PDB) and Cu(CH3CN)4BF4 possesses a stable coordination conformation with the four terminal aldehyde groups in a well-defined tetrahedral configuration. Under solvothermal conditions, the Cu(PDB)2BF4 units were connected by the imine linkages formed with linear benzidine into a weaving COF-505-Cu with the dia topology. Furthermore, Cu(I), which was located at the intersection of the two organic threads, can be removed by heating COF-505-Cu in the KCN–CH3OH–H2O system. The demetalated COF-505 has a flexible structure with a high degree of freedom, and thus, leading to a more elastic COF-505 than COF-505-Cu. In addition, treatment of COF-505 with Cu(CH3CN)4BF4 leads to its re-metalation without loss of crystallinity. Unfortunately, COF-505 has a two-fold interpenetrated framework structure with low porosity, which is not favorable for loading guest species and functionalization. In 2018, by using a similar synthetic method, but replacing BF4− with the bulky diphenylphosphinate anion (Ph2PO2−), COF-506-Cu was obtained in which the internal space is occupied by larger Ph2PO2−, resulting in a non-interpenetrating network.255 As expected, anionic dyes, such as methyl orange and hydroxynaphthol blue, can be encapsulated by COF-506-Cu by exchanging with Ph2PO2−. In addition, the crystallinity of COF-506 after demetalation is extremely reduced, which is clearly attributed to the fact that COF-506 has a larger internal space and is more flexible than COF-505. It is interesting to note that the replacement of the metal ions in COF-505 and COF-506 may endow them with novel properties; this is currently under investigation.256,257
 Fig. 8  Woven COFs based on 1,10-phenanthroline. (A) COF-505-Cu and COF-506-Cu with weaving 1D threads. Adapted with permission of ref. 255. Copyright © 2018 American Chemical Society. (B) COF-500-Cu and COF-500 with interlocking 1D square ribbons. Adapted with permission of ref. 258. Copyright © 2018 American Chemical Society. 
Additionally, the same group also examined the assembly of tetrahedral cationic Cu(PDB)2+ with rectangular tetraamino-substituted monomers.258 As shown in Fig. 8B, the 60° angle between the two aldehyde groups in Cu(PDB)2PO2Ph2 and the 120° angle between the two amino groups of 4′,4′′′,4′′′′′,4′′′′′′′-(ethene-1,1,2,2-tetrayl)tetrakis(([1,1′-biphenyl]-4-amine)) are well complementary, resulting in the formation of quadrilateral macrocycles. These macrocycles are connected by CC double bonds in the rectangular monomers, further leading to corner-sharing 1D square ribbons. The two 1D square ribbons are interlocked via the Cu(I)–biphenanthroline node in an orthogonal manner, thus yielding a woven 3D COF with pts topology.
Furthermore, the combination of two tetrahedral metal-complexes can also afford woven COFs (Fig. 9A). By imine condensation between amino- and methylal-functionalized Cu(I)–1,10-phenanthroline complexes, wCOF-Cu with a 3D weaving network was synthesized by Loh et al.259 Its crystal structure was determined by combining 3D electron diffraction and PXRD data, and it was found that wCOF-Cu crystallizes in dia topology with a 3-fold interpenetrated structure. Interestingly, the dynamic ligand exchange between homoleptic complexes and another ligand led to heteroleptic complexes, in which two kinds of functional groups are essential to complete the synthetic reaction of COFs, enabling the formation of a 1D metallopolymer. Based on this strategy, wCOF-Cu was synthesized by ligand exchange–imine condensation between bis[4,4′-(1,10-phenanthroline-2,9-diyl)dianiline]copper(I) tetrafluoroborate and 2,9-bis(4-(dimethoxymethyl)phenyl)-1,10-phenanthroline. Structurally, the 1D zigzag chains consisting of bis(2,9-diphenyl-1,10-phenanthroline)copper(I) structural units linked by imine bonds are stacked via the hydrogen bonding between amine groups and tetrafluoroborate anions and the π–π stacking of the adjacent phenanthroline plane to form mCOF-Cu. Due to the existence of amine-enriched channels in mCOF-Cu, Pt(II) can be easily immobilized inside through N–Pt interaction to afford heterobimetallic Pt/mCOF-Cu for potential catalytic application.
 Fig. 9  (A) Synthesis of 3D wCOF-Cu and 1D mCOF-Cu via imine condensation and in situ ligand exchange–imine condensation reactions. Adapted with permission of ref. 259. Copyright © 2020 Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. (B) Glyoxal as a crosslinking agent for the conversion reaction of mCOF-Ag to wCOF-Ag. Hydrogen atoms are omitted for clarity. Adapted from ref. 260 under the terms of the Creative Commons CC BY 4.0 license. Copyright © 2020, The Author(s). Published by Springer Nature. 
Furthermore, mCOF-Ag,260 an isostructural analogue of mCOF-Cu, has also been obtained from AgBF4, 2,9-bis(4-(dimethoxymethyl)phenyl)-1,10-phenanthroline, and 4,4′-(1,10-phenanthroline-2,9-diyl)dianiline through in situ metal–ligand coordination and subsequent imine condensation reaction. The free amino groups in mCOF-Ag can be cross-linked with glyoxal to form 3D wCOF-Ag (Fig. 9B), and the covalent cross-linked structure formed in this process leads to the increased Young's modulus of wCOF-Ag.
Besides V-shaped 2,9-disubstituted-1,10-phenanthrolines, linear 3,8-disubstituted-1,10-phenanthrolines can also be used for the construction of metalated COFs. Very recently, Mas-Ballesté and Alemán et al. reported the 3,8-disubstituted-1,10-phenanthroline-based Phen-COF by the reaction of 4,4′-(1,10-phenanthroline-3,8-diyl)dibenzaldehyde with 1,3,5-tris(4-aminophenyl)benzene under solvothermal conditions (1,4-dioxane/mesitylene, acetic acid, 120 °C, 3 days) (Fig. 10).261,262 Phen-COF crystallizes in the Amm2 space group with a layered eclipsed structure. The phenanthroline moiety in Phen-COF is a potential chelating site that can coordinate with a variety of metal ions via post-synthetic metalation. For example, by the combination of Phen-COF with palladium acetate in acetonitrile/water at 70 °C, 26 mol% of the phenanthrolines are chelated with Pd(II) and the palladium content is up to 4.4 wt%.262 In addition to homometalation, the authors also reported the heterometalation of Phen-COF. By the reaction of tetrakis[2-(2,4-difluorophenyl)-5-(trifluoromethyl)pyridine-C2′,N](μ-dichloro)diiridium(III) and dichloro(dimethoxyethane)nickel(II) with Phen-COF under the given conditions, the iridium(III)- and nickel(II)-coexistent Phen-COF was generated, in which 15 and 30 mol% of the phenanthrolines coordinate with the iridium(III) and nickel(II) ions, respectively.261
 Fig. 10  Phenanthroline-based COFs as effective platforms for Ir(III), Ni(II), and Pd(II) coordination. 


2.1.6. 1H-Pyrazole. 
In addition to homometallic and heterometallic COFs, the COFs from functionalized polynuclear complex monomers have also been reported recently (Fig. 11). A representative example was reported by Li and co-workers in 2021.263 By the combination of tris(4-formyl-μ2-pyrazolato-N,N′)tricopper(I) (Cu3Pz3) and 1,3,5-tris(4-aminophenyl)benzene or 4,4′,4′′-(1,3,5-triazine-2,4,6-triyl)trianiline under solvothermal conditions (mesitylene/dioxane, acetic acid, 120 °C, 72 h), JNM-1 and JNM-2 were generated as light green solid powders. They all crystallized in the hexagonal system with the P6 space group. Structural analysis revealed that JNM-1 and JNM-2 adopt an eclipsed AA stacking mode with a pore width of approximately 18.9 Å. In addition, both JNM-1 and JNM-2 exhibited good thermostability and chemical stability toward air and water. Of note, JNM-1 and JNM-2 possessed reversible redox behavior. With the aid of an oxidant, the Cu(I) ions in JNM-1 were partly oxidized to Cu(II), and JNM-1 could be completely regenerated by treating it with 1-methylpyrrolidin-2-one at 160 °C. Furthermore, JNM-1 and JNM-2 were also prepared by the one-pot in situ reactions of 1H-pyrazole-4-carbaldehyde, Cu2O and the corresponding triamine monomers, but the materials obtained by this method contain Cu2O which is difficult to remove.
 Fig. 11  Trinuclear copper(I)–pyrazolate complex as a metalated monomer for constructing a variety of metalated COFs. 
Later on, a different imine-linked 2D COF based on the same aldehyde-functionalized trinuclear copper(I)-complex with a diamine monomer was reported.264 As shown, the mechanochemical reaction of Cu3Pz3 and benzene-1,4-diamine with p-toluenesulfonic acid monohydrate in trace water and subsequent heat treatment at 170 °C afforded FDM-71. Further analysis showed that vacancy defects are present in FDM-71 due to the missing monomers, leading to the presence of unreacted amino and aldehyde groups in the scaffold, consistent with the obtained FT-IR and ssNMR spectra.
In addition, Li et al. revealed that the stacking mode of Cu3Pz3-based COFs is acid-dependent, which is rarely observed in reticular chemistry.265 With the aid of trifluoroacetic acid and acetic acid, the solvothermal reactions of Cu3Pz3 with anthracene-2,6-diamine in mesitylene/dioxane led to AA-stacked JNM-3-AA and ABC-stacked JNM-3-ABC, respectively. Interestingly, immersion of JNM-3-ABC in trifluoroacetic acid could trigger a stacking mode transformation from ABC to AA within 30 min, while the soaking of JNM-3-AA in a methanol solution of sodium methoxide could not trigger this structural transformation, indicating that strong interlayer Cu⋯Cu interactions facilitate the formation of eclipsed stacking mode based on the computational simulations.


2.1.7. Catecholate. 
It is well-known that the o-dihydroxy on catechol (viz. 1,2-dihydroxybenzene) provides an open chelate site for metal ion binding. In 2014, Jiang and co-workers demonstrated that the catechol moiety could be introduced into the COFs.266 Recently, by solvothermal reactions of 2,3-dihydroxyterephthalaldehyde with 4,4′,4′′-(1,3,5-triazine-2,4,6-triyl)trianiline, 4,4′,4′′,4′′′-(pyrene-1,3,6,8-tetrayl)tetraaniline, and 4,4′,4′′,4′′′-(ethene-1,1,2,2-tetrayl)tetraaniline, Ma and Zhao et al. successfully synthesized the TAPT-2,3-DHTA COF,267 the PyTTA-2,3-DHTA COF,268 and COF-ETTA-2,3-Dha,269 respectively, in which the coordination sites are ordered on the pore walls and structurally predesignable for binding metal ions (Fig. 12). For example, the TAPT-2,3-DHTA COF and the PyTTA-2,3-DHTA COF can be further metalated by bis(2,4-pentanedionato)vanadium(IV) oxide in an inert atmosphere (50 °C, 24 h) to yield oxyvanadium(IV)-loaded VO-TAPT-2,3-DHTA and VO-PyTTA-2,3-DHTA with 4.9 and 3.8 wt% of vanadium, respectively.267,268 The vibrational peak at 970 cm−1 in the FT-IR spectra clearly supports the existence of the VO bonds, while X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) and electron spin resonance (ESR) analyses demonstrate the oxidation state of V to be +4. Furthermore, COF-ETTA-2,3-Dha with a heteropore structure was used as an efficient adsorbent to adsorb Cd(II) from water based on the Cd–O interaction, showing saturation adsorption capacity as high as 116 mg g−1.269
 Fig. 12  Post-synthetic metalation of catechol-based COFs. (A) 2,3-Dihydroxyterephthalaldehyde as a monomer for the construction of COFs. (B) Coordination reaction of catechol-based COFs and oxovanadium(IV) acetylacetonate. 
Moreover, monomer-exchange on the established COF is also a useful approach to access the COFs with open docking sites. For example, Tang and co-workers introduced 3,4-dihydroxybenzaldehyde into COF-LZU1 by solvent-assisted monomer-exchange.270 The original benzene-1,3,5-tricarbaldehyde in the COF-skeleton was partially replaced by 3,4-dihydroxybenzaldehyde to afford defective LZU-OH with a catechol moiety. As expected, the obtained LZU-OH can bind metal ions to afford the metalated LZU-OM (M = Fe, Mn, V).
More recently, Gu et al. demonstrated that the Ti(IV)–catechol complex can also be used to construct titanium-metalated COFs (Fig. 13).96 The octahedral titanium complex Na2Ti(2,3-DHTA)3 with C3 symmetry, which was synthesized in acetonitrile by the reaction of 2,3-dihydroxyterephthalaldehyde and bis(acetylacetonato)oxotitanium(IV), reacted with 4,4′,4′′,4′′′-(pyrene-1,3,6,8-tetrayl)tetraaniline under solvothermal conditions (mesitylene/o-dichlorobenzene/acetonitrile, acetic acid, 120 °C, 7 days) to afford the desired Ti-COF-1. Ti-COF-1 is an anionic framework with Na(I) as the equilibrium cation. Ti-COF-1 with the I23 space group has an edge-transitive (6,4)-connected net, in which the [TiO6] clusters occupy eight vertices and the pyrene-1,3,6,8-tetrayltetrakis(benzene-4,1-diyl) moiety serves as the six faces to form [Ti8] cubic cages with a pore diameter of 14 Å. Every four [Ti8] cubic cages are separated by two perpendicular channels with a diameter of 16 Å to generate a 3D reticular structure with the soc topology. Consistent with its microporous framework, Ti-COF-1 shows a typical type I N2 adsorption and desorption isotherm with a BET specific surface area of 1000 m2 g−1 and a pore size of 1.55 nm.
 Fig. 13  Titanium-based anionic framework Ti-COF-1. (A) Synthesis of Ti-COF-1. (B) Structure of Ti-COF-1. The filled yellow spheres and the blue polyhedra indicate two types of pores with different chemical environments. Adapted with permission of ref. 96. Copyright © 2021 Wiley-VCH GmbH. 


2.1.8. Triphenylphosphine. 
Triphenylphosphine (PPh3), a common ligand in organometallic chemistry, has only recently been employed for COF metalation.271,272 Two examples of P(III)-containing COFs, P-COF-1 and P-COF-2, were synthesized by Fan and co-workers via the reaction of 4,4′,4′′-phosphanetriyltribenzaldehyde with benzene-1,4-diamine or benzidine under solvothermal conditions.273 Theoretically, due to the presence of a lone electron pair on P, COF-1 and P-COF-2 readily coordinate with acetylacetonatodicarbonylrhodium(I) to form Rh–P-COF-1 and Rh–P-COF-2. The vibrational absorption due to the Rh–P bond was observed at 442 cm−1 by FT-IR spectroscopy, suggesting the interaction of Rh-species with P. Although the coordination mode and distribution of Rh(I) with the COFs have not been fully investigated, this provides a possible way for enriching the range of applications of COFs as supramolecular ligands.


2.1.9. N-Heterocyclic carbene (NHC). 
In addition to the metal–heteroatom coordination, the organometallic metal–carbon coordination can also be used to realize COF metalation. As we know, NHCs are classified as stable nitrogen heterocyclic compounds characterized by a divalent carbon atom with a six-electron valence shell.274 Due to their distinct σ-donor properties, NHCs are widely employed as ligands to bind transition metals to access NHC–metal complexes (NHC–M).275 An unavoidable challenge in constructing COFs with NHC or NHC–M monomers is their stability under solvothermal conditions.276
Recently, Dong et al. reported a NHC–AuCl-COF by direct polymerization of chloro[1,3-diethyl-4,7-bis(4-formylphenyl)-2,3-dihydro-1H-benzo[d]imidazol-2-ylidene]gold(I) with 4,4′,4′′-(1,3,5-triazine-2,4,6-triyl)trianiline under solvothermal conditions (Fig. 14A).277 The obtained NHC–AuCl-COF possesses a staggered AB stacking mode with a pore size of 2.8 nm. Of note, the Au content in NHC–AuCl-COF is up to 23.4 wt%, which is very close to the theoretical value of 24.1 wt%, implying that the NHC–Au moiety is stable under solvothermal conditions. The only existence of Au(I) rather than Au(0) in NHC–AuCl-COF, which is determined by XPS, scanning electron microscopy (SEM), and transmission electron microscopy (TEM), further supported the above presumption. The direct polymerization of NHC–M monomers for synthesis of metalated COFs ensures not only a high loading content of NHC–M species but also their uniform distribution in the COF matrix.
 Fig. 14  NHC–M-based COFs. (A) Synthesis of NHC–AuCl-COF using the NHC–Au-loaded complex as a monomer. (B) Synthesis of COF-NHC–Pd via post-synthetic metalation. 
Compared to direct synthesis, post-synthetic metalation is also a practical approach to access NHC–M-based COFs. Using this strategy, Wang et al. reported a NHC–Pd(II)-loaded COF with pre-embedded imidazolium (Fig. 14B).278 Specifically, the ionothermal reaction of 1,1′-((4,4′′-diformyl-[1,1′:4′,1′′-terphenyl]-2′,5′-diyl)bis(methylene))bis(3-propyl-1H-imidazol-3-ium) hexafluorophosphate with benzene-1,3,5-triamine at room temperature generated COF-NHC, which after combination with palladium acetate in acetonitrile at 75 °C for 3 h afforded the NHC–Pd(II)-loaded COF-NHC–Pd with a Pd content of up to 20.1 wt%. Other types of NHC–M such as NHC–Ru can also be introduced into the COF-frameworks by this method, which was reported by Lotsch and co-workers recently.279


2.1.10. Dehydrobenzoannulene. 
Metal–carbon π-complexes are valuable raw materials for many synthetic reactions and key intermediates in various catalytic processes.280 Although they have been known from the early days in organometallic chemistry, they have only recently been integrated into COFs.
McGrier et al. first reported 2D COFs containing C3-symmetric π-conjugated planar triangular dehydrobenzoannulenes which are potential sites for metal binding via π–d interactions.281,282 Later on, the McGrier group reported that the polymerization of (methanetetrayltetrakis(benzene-4,1-diyl))tetraboronic acid and 5,6,11,12,17,18-hexadehydro-2,3,8,9,14,15-hexahydroxytribenzo[a,e,i]cyclododecene generated the green DBA-3D-COF with a bor topological network (Fig. 15).138 As an electron-rich COF-ligand, DBA-3D-COF can be further metalated by the reaction with bis(1,5-cyclooctadiene)nickel(0) to afford purple Ni-DBA-3D-COF but without loss of its structural feature and crystallinity. Spectroscopy analysis indicated that Ni-DBA-3D-COF displayed an additional charge-transfer absorption band at 500–650 nm, implying that the alkynyl provided 2e− to form a 16-electron complex. Moreover, the fluorescence of DBA-3D-COF at 510 nm was quenched after metalation, further supporting the formation of a Ni(0) complex.
 Fig. 15  Nickel(0)-coordinated hexadehydrotribenzo[12]annulene-based Ni-DBA-3D-COF. Hydrogen atoms are omitted for clarity. COD, (1Z,5Z)-cycloocta-1,5-diene. 
Similarly, in 2020, the same group reported that DBA-2D-COF constructed from 5,6,11,12,17,18-hexadehydro-2,8,14-triformyltribenzo[a,e,i]cyclododecene and hydrazine was also used as a COF-ligand for Ni(0) loading.283 After treatment with bis(1,5-cyclooctadiene)nickel(0) in toluene, approximately 64 mol% of dehydrobenzoannulenes in DBA-2D-COF were metalated as the Ni(0)–triethyne complex.

2.2. Metal–linkage coordination
In addition to organic ligand-based COF metalation, the electron-enriched COF-linkages, such as imine, β-ketoenamine, and acylhydrazone, can also act as the active coordination sites for metal binding to access COF metalation (Fig. 16). This approach might overcome to some extent the limitation of the aforementioned COF metalation methods, but the precise locations and coordination modes for the loaded metals in COF-frameworks sometimes cannot be clearly demonstrated.
 Fig. 16  Coordinate interaction of metal ions with the linkages of COFs. 

2.2.1. Imine linkage. 
Since the first report of COF-300 in 2009,33 imine-linked COFs have become the most abundant and well-studied subclass of COFs. Imine bonds have abundant reaction chemistry and their various chemical transformations are an effective approach to realize the further functionalization of imine-linked COFs.284 Besides, the regularly arranged imine linkage in COF-frameworks provides useful coordination sites for COF metalation by imine–metal coordination.
In a pioneering work by Wang et al. in 2011,129 the imine-linked COF-LZU1 was successfully metalated by Pd(II) via mixing of Pd(CH3COO)2 with COF-LZU1 in dichloromethane for 24 h under ambient conditions. The authors demonstrated that the loaded Pd(II) ions (7.1 wt%) are located between the 2D COF-layers and fixed by the interlayer N–Pd–N interactions in Pd/COF-LZU1 (type I in Fig. 16). The Pd(II) bonding energy by XPS is 337.7 eV, similar to that of diacetato(1,10-phenanthroline)palladium(II) (337.8 eV), but lower than that of Pd(CH3COO)2 (338.4 eV). Later on, Jiang and co-workers used a similar method to load Pd(II) in H2P-Bph-COF with a Pd content of 12.9 wt%.285
The rationality of this coordination mode was further bolstered by subsequent research. In 2021, Karim et al. reported PdCl2@ILCOF-1 and studied the local coordination and electronic property of Pd(II) in ILCOF-1 (Fig. 17).286 The obtained PdCl2@ILCOF-1 product is a dark brown powder with a Pd content of 18.1% based on ICP–OES analysis. X-ray absorption near-edge structure (XANES) spectra at the Pd K-edge showed that the spectral pattern of PdCl2@ILCOF-1 is quite different from that of PdO, while it is similar but still not identical to that of PdCl2. The extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) spectra suggested that Pd(II) is bound to two N and two Cl atoms at the distances of 2.31 Å and 2.03 Å, respectively, revealing that Pd(II) lies in a tetracoordinated sphere. Furthermore, based on the diffuse-reflectance FT-IR spectrum, the adsorption of CO by PdCl2@ILCOF-1 at −40 °C only resulted in a narrow peak at 2130 cm−1 with a full width at half maximum of approximately 20 cm−1 with no other CO band observed, strongly suggesting a single local coordination environment for Pd(II) in PdCl2@ILCOF-1.
 Fig. 17  Pd(II) between adjacent layers of imine-linked ILCOF-1. (A) Metalation of ILCOF-1. (B) The k3-weighted χ(R) Pd K-edge EXAFS spectra of PdCl2@ILCOF-1, PdCl2, and PdO. (C) Diffuse-reflectance FT-IR spectrum of CO adsorbed on PdCl2@ILCOF-1 at −40 °C. Adapted from ref. 286 under the terms of the Creative Commons CC BY-NC-ND 4.0 license. Copyright © 2021, The Author(s). Published by Elsevier Inc. 
When Pd(II) is doped into COFs by the one-pot method, the coordination mode of Pd(II) differs from that of post-synthetic metalation. Investigation of the TAPB-BTCA COF prepared by [3+3] condensation of 1,3,5-tris(4-aminophenyl)benzene and benzene-1,3,5-tricarbaldehyde showed that with the increase of local defects (e.g., –NH2) in the COF, Pd(II) tends to simultaneously coordinate with the amino N and imine N between the adjacent layers (type II in Fig. 16) rather than with imine N exclusively.287 Given the prevalence of defects in COFs, this may provide a new perspective for the optimization of the in situ and post-synthetic metalation of COFs.
In fact, the COF–metal coordination, which largely depends on the metal coordination preference and the coordinating nature of COF-ligands, is complicated. For example, the loaded Pt(II) ions in COF-UARK-49-Pt288 are located in a planar quadrilateral coordination environment formed by two Cl−, one DMSO, and one imine N donors (type III in Fig. 16). Furthermore, during the post-synthetic metalation of Py-1P with [Cp*IrCl2]2 (Cp* = pentamethylcyclopentadienyl),289 the authors found that the loaded Ir(III) not only coordinates to imine N and Cp* ring, but also forms a C–Ir bond with the phenyl ring attached to imine in Py-1P-Ir (type IV in Fig. 16). All these observations were respectively reported by Moghadam288 and Beyzavi289 groups very recently.
In addition, the bisimine-assisted metalation has been reported recently (type V in Fig. 16). In 2021, Van Der Voort et al. found that the bisimine-functionalized Ace-COF could be readily metalated by simple post-synthetic wet impregnation with NiCl2 under ambient conditions with a Ni content of 1.0 mmol g−1.290 XPS analysis elucidated the interaction between N and Ni(II). Upon the introduction of Ni(II), the N 1s XPS peak shifts toward higher binding energy, and the Ni 2p peak is located at 856 eV and is distinguished from the Ni(0) and NiO peaks.
The electron-rich substituents, e.g., hydroxyl and phenolate (type VI in Fig. 16), on the monomer adjacent to the imine can participate in metal ion coordination to provide the chelating coordination sites for binding metal ions to achieve COF metalation. For example, by refluxing RIO-12 with NiCl2 in ethanol with K2CO3, Esteves and co-workers successfully synthesized NiCl@RIO-12 with 3.6–25 wt% of Ni(II) by varying the NiCl2 dosage.291 Using the same approach, Ji et al. reported a Pd(II)-decorated Pd/COF-BTDH.292 The research demonstrated that both imine nitrogen and hydroxy oxygen were coordinated to Pd(II) inside the pores and the ordered channel structure played an important role in regulating the regioselectivity for the oxidative Heck reaction. In addition to Ni(II) and Pd(II), the Cu(II) grafting on this type of COF can also be realized. In 2020, Gao and co-workers reported the Cu@T-D COF by metalating the (E)-1-((phenylimino)methyl)naphthalen-2-ol moiety in the T-D COF.293 Since the T-D COF contains pyridyl donors, the definite location of Cu(II) deserves further study.

N,N′-Bis(salicylidene)ethylenediamino (salen), containing an N,N′,O,O′-planar coordination pocket, is an important class of bisimine ligands formed by 2-hydroxybenzaldehyde and ethylenediamine at a molar ratio of 2:1. A variety of metal ions, e.g., Cu(II), Zn(II), Fe(III), Al(III), V(IV), and Sn(IV), can be readily embedded in the salen pocket, which yields tetradentate MN2O2 or pentadentate MN2O2A (M = metal ion, A = axial ligand) metallosalen.294 Due to the strong ability to accommodate metal ions, the COFs generated from salen monomers are an ideal class of platforms to realize metalation of COFs. In 2017, Wang et al. first reported the salen-linked COFs and their post-synthetic metalation (type VII in Fig. 16).295 As shown in Fig. 18A, Salen-COF1 was prepared by the imine condensation of C3-symmetric salicylaldehyde with ethylenediamine under solvothermal conditions (dioxane/ethanol, acetic acid, 120 °C, 3 days). The structural analysis indicated that the AA stacked 2D salen-COF crystallized in the P321 space group with an interlayer spacing of 3.4 Å. Due to the large BET specific surface area (1366 m2 g−1), pore volume (0.73 cm3 g−1), and pore size (2.5 nm), Salen-COFs allow the metal ions to diffuse into the COF-framework and trap them by the salen linkage. As expected, a series of metal ions, including Cu(II), Ni(II), Zn(II), Co(II), and Mn(II), can be loaded on Salen-COF1 in the ratio of 64–88% under given conditions, indicating that Salen-COF1 is an ideal platform for metal ion immobilization. Of note, the oxidation of Co(II)-loaded salen-COF with air led to the formation of Co(III)-loaded salen-COF that is difficult to be prepared by direct impregnation due to the unavailability of Co(III) salts.296
 Fig. 18  Salen and salphen skeletons for fixing metal ions. (A) Synthesis of metalated salen-based COFs via post-synthetic metalation. (B) Synthesis of metalated salen-based chiral COFs (CCOFs) via in situ self-assembly and post-synthetic metal exchange. (C) Synthesis of metallosalphen-based 3D COFs via post-synthetic metalation. 
In addition to post-synthetic metalation, metal ions can also be introduced into the salen moiety by the one-pot in situ method while forming COFs. The involved metal ions may serve as a template to facilitate COF formation and crystallization. In 2017, Cui and co-workers presented such an example, in which 1,3,5-tri(3-formyl-4-hydroxyphenyl)benzene or 1,3,5-tri(3-(tert-butyl)-5-formyl-4-hydroxyphenyl)benzene, zinc acetate, and (1R,2R)-cyclohexane-1,2-diamine were employed to synthesize Zn(II)-loaded chiral CCOF3 and CCOF4 (Fig. 18B).297 CCOF4 is chemically more stable than CCOF3 due to the steric hindrance of tert-butyl, and shows a wide range of reaction chemistry. For example, when CCOF4 is immersed in saturated solutions of metal salts—such as CrCl2, Fe(CH3COO)2, Mn(CH3COO)2, bis(2,4-pentanedionato)vanadium(IV), and Co(CH3COO)2—the target ions underwent ion exchange with Zn(II) along with an oxidation process—except for V(IV)—to afford a series of heterobimetallic CCOF4-M (M = Cr(III), Co(III), Mn(III), Fe(III), V(IV)) with the Zn(II) to M ratio in the range of 1:12 to 1:54. The residual Zn(II) in CCOF4-Cr(III) can be further exchanged by M′ to give heterotrimetallic CCOF4-Cr-M′ (M′ = Fe(III), Mn(III), Co(III)). In addition, V(IV) in CCOF4-V was oxidized to V(V) by 3-chlorobenzoperoxoic acid. During ion exchange processes, the structural integrity and crystallinity of these chiral salen-COFs are maintained. Furthermore, the Zn(II)-metalated 3D salen-COFs with a seven-fold interpenetrating structure were also reported by the same group in 2019.298
The analogue of salen, N,N′-bis(salicylideneimine)-1,2-diaminobenzo (salphen), has also been used to construct metalated 3D COFs (type VIII in Fig. 16). As reported by Fang et al. in 2019,299 the non-interpenetrated dia salphen-based JUC-509 COF, obtained by the assembly of 4,5-dichlorobenzene-1,2-diamine with 5,5′,5′′,5′′′-methanetetrayltetrakis(2-hydroxybenzaldehyde) under solvothermal conditions (mesitylene/dioxane, acetic acid, 120 °C, 3 days), can be metalated by Mn(II), Cu(II), and Eu(III) via post-synthetic wet impregnation (Fig. 18C). Furthermore, Gu et al. recently reported a heteropore salphen-COFHATP-DMDBvia the solvothermal reaction of triphenylene-2,3,6,7,10,11-hexaamine and 4,6-dihydroxy-5-methylisophthalaldehyde. As expected, it can bind Ni(II) by the salphen moiety to form Ni-Salphen-COFHATP-DMDB with hexagonal and quadrilateral pores, and the four-coordinated Ni(II) ions are located on the hexagonal pore walls (Fig. 19).300
 Fig. 19  Synthesis of salphen-based COFs with hexagonal and quadrilateral pores. (A) Schematic diagram of Salphen-COFHATP-DMDB. (B) Schematic diagram of Ni-Salphen-COFHATP-DMDB. 
In addition, the participation of the neighboring groups in coordination is also observed in the COFs containing pyridine rings. In 2020, Zhao and co-workers reported a series of metalated COFs based on COF-DB.301 As shown in Fig. 20, the pyridin-2-ylmethanimino linkage in the framework provides the N,N′-bidentate chelating site on the same side that can trap metal ions (type IX in Fig. 16). As a result, a variety of metal ions such as Cu(II), Co(II), Ni(II), Pd(II), Zn(II), Mn(II), and Cd(II) are embedded in the COF-scaffold, leading to a blueshift in the stretching vibration of the CN bond from 1655 cm−1 to 1657–1663 cm−1. In addition, the metal-coordination further limits the rotation of the C–C bond between the pyridyl and the imine bond, making an additional contribution to the stabilization of the framework that is reflected in the increased BET specific surface area. Furthermore, as evidenced by the study of Van Der Voort et al., rare earth ions can also coordinate with TTA-DFP-COF by the pyridin-2-ylmethanimino moiety.302 By adjusting the ratio of Eu(III) (red luminescence) and Tb(III) (green luminescence), together with the inherent blue luminescence of TTA-DFP-COF, a composite luminescent material with white light emission is achieved.
 Fig. 20  Hydrazone-linked COF-DB containing the pyridin-2-ylmethanimino bridge for chelating metal ions. (A) Syntheses of COF-DB and metalated M/COF-DB. (B) Schematic diagram of interlayer and intralayer hydrogen bonds in COF-DB. (C) 2D small-angle X-ray scattering (SAXS) and wide-angle X-ray scattering (WAXS) patterns of the COF-DB powder. (D) PXRD patterns of M/COF-DB. Adapted with permission of ref. 301. Copyright © 2020 American Chemical Society. 
Additionally, the N,N′,N′′-tridentate coordination site in the pyridine-2,6-dicarbaldehyde (PyDA)-derived imine-linked COFs was also reported (type X in Fig. 16). One such impressive example was observed in the Co-based woven COF-112 that was reported by Yaghi and co-workers in 2017 (Fig. 21).13 The cascade reaction of PyDA, tert-butyl (4-aminophenyl)carbamate (NBPDA) and Co(BF4)2 at 85 °C in acetonitrile/toluene produced COF-112 with dia net: first, the bis(imino)pyridine ligand 1 generated from imine condensation of PyDA with NBPDA coordinated to Co(II) to form precursor 2; then, the CF3COOH-assisted tert-butyloxy carbonyl hydrolysis gave the key intermediate 3; finally, the amino group in 3 was guided by the Co(II) to form interlaced 1D polyimine chains with PyDA via imine condensation, leading to the formation of COF-112 with a woven structure. In this process, the slow hydrolysis of the tert-butyloxy carbonyl group allows the cobalt coordination reaction to occur prior to the imine bond formation. This enables Co(II) with six-coordinated tetragonal bipyramidal geometry to act as a template to guide the lengthening and weaving of the molecular chains. By contrast, attempts to substitute NBPDA with p-phenylenediamine only yielded 1D polyimine, because the imine condensation reaction is faster than metal coordination and cannot provide a regular woven structure. Not surprisingly, pre-synthesis of Co-complex 3 followed by reaction with PyDA and Co(II) also afford COF-112 as small and aggregated microcrystals. It is worth mentioning that the oxidation of COF-112 with NaClO2 can convert the imine bond to the amide bond, while the Co oxidation state remains intact.303 Furthermore, COF-112-Fe, the iron-based analogue of COF-112, was also synthesized by a similar method. Unfortunately, neither Co(II) nor Fe(II) can be removed from the molecular chain and metal-free woven COFs cannot be obtained.13,303
 Fig. 21  Structure and synthesis of woven COF-112. (A) Synthesis of COF-112 by the one-pot and pre-prepared Co-complex methods. (B) Woven structure of COF-112. Different colors are used to represent polyimine chains with different chemical environments, and the gray balls represent cobalt(II) ions. Inset: Coordination environment of Co(II). 


2.2.2. β-Ketoenamine linkage. 
The carbonyl O and enamine N connected by the CC bond in β-ketoenamine-linked COFs can provide an additional type of bidentate coordination site to bind metal ions (type XI in Fig. 16). In 2018, Cui et al. reported a β-ketoenamine-linked chiral COF, CCOF-TpTab, which after coordination to Cu(II) gave CCOF-TpTab-Cu with a Cu(II) loading of 1.2 wt%.304 Fitting of structural parameters from EXAFS spectra showed that the loaded Cu(II) coordinated to one nitrogen and three oxygen atoms. In 2021, Islama et al. reported the Pd(II)-loaded β-ketoenamine-linked TFR-OT COF.305 After coordination, the absorption peak in the FT-IR spectrum associated with the CO stretching vibration was redshifted from 1624 to 1563 cm−1 and the peak for the N–H stretching vibration broadened. The authors thought that these changes were caused by the attenuation of the CO and N–H bonds due to the electron donation of O and N after coordination.


2.2.3. Acylhydrazone linkage. 
Acylhydrazone-linked COFs formed by salicylaldehyde and hydrazide possess a unique (E)-N′-(2-hydroxybenzylidene)benzohydrazido unit in which only three of the four heteroatoms can participate in coordination as O,N,O′-type tridentate ligands because of conformational constraint (type XII in Fig. 16). In 2020, Ma et al. reported that Redox-COF1—synthesized from 2,5-dihydroxyterephthalaldehyde and benzene-1,3,5-tricarbohydrazide—can coordinate with UO22+ and subsequently undergo electron transfer from hydroxyl to UO22+, allowing the oxidation of benzene-1,4-diol to benzoquinone to achieve effective adsorption of uranium via the redox adsorption mechanism.306 The adsorption selectivity for UO22+ was up to 97% at pH = 3. Furthermore, the Bth-Dma COF, which was constructed from benzene-1,3,5-tricarbohydrazide and 2,5-dimethoxyterephthalaldehyde, has a regular arrangement of the (E)-N′-(2-methoxybenzylidene)benzohydrazido units on the pore wall that can readily bind Fe(III) in an aqueous solution, leading to the formation of O,N,O′-chelated Fe(III) along with fluorescence quenching of the Bth-Dma COF at 518 nm.307


2.2.4. β-Ketoacylhydrazone linkage. 
Similar to acylhydrazone-linked COFs, β-ketoacylhydrazone-linked COFs also provide tridentate O,N,O′-chelating sites (type XIII in Fig. 16). Recently, Dong et al. reported the gram-level synthesis of COF-DM by the reaction of 2′-methyl-[1,1′:4′,1′′-terphenyl]-4,4′′-dicarbohydrazide with 2,4,6-trihydroxybenzene-1,3,5-tricarbaldehyde in dimethyl sulfoxide/1,3,5-trimethylbenzene at 60 °C under atmospheric pressure. After mixing with CuCl2 in acetonitrile, the Cu(II)-loaded Cu(II)@COF-DM was obtained with a Cu loading of 13.0 wt% (Fig. 22).308 In order to further determine the coordination environment of Cu(II) in COF-DM, N′,N′′′,N′′′-((1E,1′E,1′′E)-(2,4,6-trioxocyclohexane-1,3,5-triylidene)tris(methaneylylidene))tri(benzohydrazide) that was generated from benzohydrazide and 2,4,6-trihydroxybenzene-1,3,5-tricarbaldehyde was used as the model molecular ligand to synthesize the Cu(II)-complex. The single-crystal analysis showed that Cu(II) in the model complex adopts [NO3] planar square coordination formed by β-ketoacylhydrazone and a coordinated methanol molecule. In addition, molybdenum-doped β-ketoacylhydrazone-COF was also reported by Zhang and co-workers recently.309
 Fig. 22  β-Ketoacylhydrazone-linked COF-DM as a reticular ligand of Cu(II). (A) Synthesis of COF-DM and Cu(II)@COF-DM. (B) Single-crystal structure of the model compound. 

2.3. Metal nanoparticle-loaded COFs
As previously mentioned, metal ions can be immobilized into COFs by either direct polymerization of metal-containing monomers or post-synthetic metalation on the established COFs with open coordination sites. Furthermore, the metal species can also be loaded by COF-carriers as nanoparticles.310
In 2012, Fischer et al. reported the first example of COFs with deposited metal nanoparticles.132 By diffusing the Pd(η3-C3H5)(η5-C5H5) gas into COF-102 in vacuum and subsequent ultraviolet light irradiation, Pd30wt%@COF-102 was obtained with the Pd nanoparticles with a size of 2.4 nm. Because COFs have a well-defined pore structure, the growth of metal nanoparticles in the COFs is spatially restricted and the metal nanoparticle aggregation can be effectively prevented during preparation and usage. As a result, the ultra-small nanoparticles loaded in COFs are easily obtained (Fig. 23). To date, the methods for preparation of the metal nanoparticle-loaded COFs can be roughly divided into three types, namely reduction, hydrolysis, and precipitation.
 Fig. 23  Synthesis of nanoparticles encapsulated in COFs by the sequence of coordination adsorption–diffusion–confined growth. 

2.3.1. Post-synthetic reduction. 
The post-synthetic reduction is a powerful and versatile method to prepare the metal or low-valent metal oxide nanoparticles loaded in COFs. The commonly used reducing agents are NaBH4, citrate, hydrogen, etc.
In 2020, Zhang and co-workers reported an imine-linked Phos-COF-1 which is equipped with triphenylphosphane coordination groups (Fig. 24).271 Due to the ordered distribution of phosphine coordination sites in the well-defined COF pores, a series of homo- and heterometallic metal nanoparticles, including Pd, Pt, Au, and PdAu, were successfully embedded in Phos-COF-1 by post-synthetic reduction with the aid of NaBH4. The COF-supported metal nanoparticles are stable, well-dispersed, and ultrafine (1–2 nm). In fact, NaBH4 is an excellent reducing agent and has been widely used in the preparation of the Pd,140,143,195,271,311–317 Ag,318–320 Ru,321 and Pt271,312,314 nanoparticles loaded in COFs.
 Fig. 24  Ultra-small metal nanoparticles embedded in the phosphine-based imine-linked COF. (A) Synthesis of Phos-COF-1. (B) HRTEM images of Phos-COF-1-supported Pd, Pt, Au, and PdAu nanoparticles. Adapted with permission of ref. 271. Copyright © 2020 WILEY-VCH Verlag GmbH & Co. KGaA, Weinheim. 
Of note, application of NaBH4 in the preparation of metal nanoparticles supported on imine-linked COFs would also cause the imine linkage reduction. For example, Deng and co-workers reported that the amine-linked COFs COF-300-AR and COF-366-M-AR can be directly synthesized by reduction of their corresponding imine-lined COFs with the aid of NaBH4 even at temperature below 0 °C.46 Therefore, its improper use might lead to amine linkage formation and sometimes a decrease in crystallinity after reduction.316 An alternative is to use a milder reducing agent instead of NaBH4 to exclude this adverse effect. For example, Wang et al. synthesized the imine-linked TAPA-TFPA-COF-supported gold nanoparticles (3.9 ± 0.5 nm) using sodium citrate as a reducing agent with the assistance of polyvidone.322 Later on, Fan et al. reduced the RuCl3 in the TpPa-1 COF by H2 in a N2 atmosphere at 280 °C to afford COF-supported Ru nanoparticles. A slight decrease in the crystallinity of TpPa-1 was observed after reduction.323 In addition, vitamin C is another weak reducing agent that has been used to prepare the COF-BD(OH)2-supported Cu nanoparticles, as reported by Islam et al. recently.324
Additionally, partial reduction of inorganic salts can give low-valent metal oxides. For example, FeCl3 in the IISERP-COF6 COF was reduced with NaBH4 to obtain Fe3O4@COF,325 while the treatment of COFs with KMnO4 led to COF-supported MnO2 nanoparticles.326,327Table 3 provides more such examples.132,133,140,143,271,311–362
