2.3.2. Post-synthetic hydrolysis. 
Post-synthetic hydrolysis is an effective approach for incorporation of metal oxides into COFs. The hydrolysis of the COF-supported metal salts in water or alkaline solutions can afford the corresponding metal oxides even though their actual structure may be extremely complex.
For example, in 2021, Pang et al. confirmed that gradual hydrolysis of tetrabutyl titanate loaded in DMTP-TAPB-COF in ethanol and water at 160 °C gave TiO2@DMTP-TAPB-COF with a TiO2 loading of up to 38.9 wt%.363 The band gap of TiO2@DMTP-TAPB-COF is 2.4 eV, which is significantly smaller than that of free TiO2 (3.2 eV), confirming the interaction between TiO2 and DMTP-TAPB-COF.
In addition, the hydrolysis of TbBd COF-supported tetrabutyl titanate in supercritical CO2 with trace water was also reported by Zhang et al.364 Compared to direct hydrolysis, the use of supercritical CO2 can effectively avoid the TiO2 aggregation during hydrolysis. More importantly, the hydrolysis in supercritical CO2 leads to the formation of O–Ti–N and N–Ti–N bonds, which was evidenced by FT-IR, XPS, and Fourier-transformed Ti K-edge EXAFS spectra. In contrast, the TiO2/TbBd COF obtained by direct hydrolysis appears to be a physical mixture of TiO2 and the TbBd COF.
As shown in Fig. 25, Minasian et al. reported the COF-5-supported actinide oxides.365 After the formation of Th(hfa)4@COF-5 and U(hfa)4@COF-5 (hfa = hexafluoroacetylacetonate) via room-temperature sublimation, the actinide oxide-loaded ThO2@COF-5 and UO2@COF-5 were obtained by hydrolysis in humid argon at 200 °C. TEM and SAXS techniques showed that ThO2 and UO2 nanoparticle growth was effectively limited by the size of COF-5 pores (2.7 nm) such that ultrasmall nanoparticle products (below 3 nm) were generated. In addition, X-ray absorption fine structure spectroscopy methods, such as XANES and EXAFS, provided information on the coordination environment, coordination number, bond length, and oxidation state.366 Specifically, actinide L3-edge XANES spectra revealed significant differences in the electronic structure, particle size, and surface chemistry between ThO2 and UO2 embedded in COF-5 and the bulk counterparts. The decrease in the peak amplitude of the EXAFS spectra indicates that ThO2 and UO2 embedded in COF-5 are more disordered with a larger bond length distribution, and have smaller particle size than the corresponding bulk materials. In addition, this study provides a useful template for the characterization of metal-containing nanoparticles in COFs.
 Fig. 25  Structural characterization of ultra-small Th(IV) and U(IV) dioxide nanoparticles embedded in COF-5. (A) Bright-field TEM and dark-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (STEM) images of ThO2@COF-5 and UO2@COF-5. (B) Left and center: SAXS patterns and their fitting results. Right: Nanoparticle size distributions based on SAXS-fitting Schulz distributions. (C) XANES and EXAFS spectra of ThO2@COF-5 and UO2@COF-5. Adapted from ref. 365 under the terms of the Creative Commons CC BY-NC 3.0 license. Copyright © 2020, The Royal Society of Chemistry.

2.3.3. Post-synthetic sedimentation. 
Metal ions coordinated to COFs can also be converted to solvent-insoluble nanoparticles by precipitating agents. In 2021, Caro et al. reported the synthesis of ZIF-67@TpPa-1; here, the TpPa-1 COF grown on porous α-Al2O3 was immersed vertically in a Co(NO3)2 solution to immobilize Co(II) through coordination, and 2-methyl-1H-imidazole was subsequently added to the reaction system that diffused in the pores and reacted with Co(II) to form ZIF-67 by rapid nucleation and restricted growth within the pores.371 Since the size of a single sod cage of ZIF-67 (1.70 nm) is smaller than the pore size of TpPa-1 (1.83 nm), ZIF-67 can form particles with only one cage size inside the pores of TpPa-1 COF. Unfortunately, attempts to observe ZIF-67 in ZIF-67@TpPa-1 by HRTEM were unsuccessful, most likely due to the poor stability of ultrasmall ZIF-67 under high-energy electron beams. Moreover, ZIF-8@TpPa-1 and ZIF-67@TpBD can also be prepared by a similar method. It is important to mention that in the fabrication of MOF/COF composites, this two-step method of metal coordination–ligand addition is significantly different from the one-step method that involves immersing COFs in a mixed solution of metal ions and ligands and heating them. The two-step method usually leads to the growth of MOFs within the pores of the COFs, whereas the one-step method usually results in a core–shell or layer-by-layer structure.372
By a two-step precursor addition strategy, perovskite@COF nanocomposites were prepared by Mukherjee et al. in 2021.373 After the reaction of EB-COF:Br with PbBr2 in DMF solution (60 °C, 2 h), the generated Pb(II)-coordinated EB-COF:Br was combined with CsBr in toluene/CH3OH at 60 °C for 5 min to afford CsPbBr3/Cs4PbBr6 perovskite@COF nanocomposites. PXRD analysis showed that the crystallinity of EB-COF:Br was retained during the synthesis process and the phase component of the perovskite depended on the concentrations of PbBr2 and CsBr. It was found that the EB-COF:Br shell greatly improved the water stability of interior perovskites. The same year, Wang and co-workers reported perovskite quantum dots doped in COF-SH for facilitating light-harvesting and promoting light-converting applications.374
In addition, COF-supported transition metal carbonate, sulfide and phosphate nanoparticles have also been synthesized recently. In 2020, Dong and co-workers demonstrated that CaCO3 nanoparticles can also be embedded in nanoscale TPB-DMTP-COF through the sequential treatment of CaCl2 and NH4HCO3, with a CaCO3 content of up to 35.3 wt%.375 Due to the hydrophobicity and protective effect of the shell, the decomposition of CaCO3 under weakly acidic conditions is slowed down. Later on, the nanoscale SnS2-loaded SnS2/TpPa-1 heterojunction was reported by Shi et al.376 More recently, Wang and co-workers prepared the Ag3PO4@TpPa-1 COF for photocatalytic detoxification of hazardous pesticides in a similar manner.377
Sometimes, post-synthetic sedimentation might cause solid-phase transformation, leading to the formation of new nanoparticles in COFs, which was reported by Pang and co-workers recently. For example, treating the Cu(II)-loaded LZU-1 COF with Se2− in solution afforded CuSe@LZU-1,142 which after further treatment with the Tollens reagent gave Ag2Se@LZU-1.378 Both XPS and PXRD analysis showed that CuSe has been completely transformed into Ag2Se. However, the direct treatment of the Ag(I)-loaded LZU-1 COF with Se2− in solution only afforded silver nanorods, possibly because the coordination interaction of Ag(I) with LZU-1 is weaker than that of Cu(II).

3. Application of metalated COFs
Metalated COFs integrate the high stability of covalent bonding with the flexibility of coordination bonding, giving them the properties of both COFs and metal species, such as modularity, regular structure, permanent porosity, high mechanical strength, low density, high activity, customizability, and scalability. These characteristics undoubtedly endow them with many applications, including adsorption and separation, energy storage, electrocatalysis, photocatalysis, thermocatalysis, sensing and analysis, and biomedicine applications. However, their relatively poor processability and high-cost synthesis might limit their practical applications.379 Therefore, their low-cost large-scale production and feasible processing methods are the imperative but challenging tasks.
Unlike the previous section, which focused on the design and synthesis of metalated COFs, this section will focus on the applications of metalated COFs.
3.1. Adsorption and separation

3.1.1. Gas adsorption and separation. 
Hydrogen has long been considered to be one of the cleanest energy sources, but its practical use still faces significant barriers due to storage difficulties. Other combustible gases, such as methane, ethane, ethylene, and carbon monoxide, are important chemical feedstocks. In addition, carbon dioxide emissions contribute to the greenhouse effect and global warming that are serious environmental problems facing mankind today. High concentrations of nitrogen oxides and sulfur dioxide are toxic to humans, animals, and plants. Therefore, the development of practical methods for selective gas adsorption and storage is an urgent but challenging task. Selective gas adsorption by porous materials is one of the strategies developed to date for achieving this goal.111,380,381
As an emerging class of crystalline porous materials, COFs have been proposed for gas adsorption382–384 and separation.385–388 Various theoretical and experimental studies have demonstrated that COFs have high gas storage capacity at low temperature and high pressure, but their storage capacity at ambient temperature and pressure is not yet satisfactory.389–392 For example, COF-108, a well-known storage material for molecular hydrogen, has gravimetric hydrogen uptake capacity as high as 21 wt% at 100 bar and 77 K. However, upon increasing the temperature to 298 K, the hydrogen uptake plummeted to 4.5 wt%, even at a high pressure of 100 bar.393 The hydrogen uptake capacity is even less than 1 wt% at near normal temperature and pressure,394 indicating that COFs are still far from practical application. Structurally, the pore size (1–5 nm) of 2D COFs is much larger than the kinetic diameters of common gas molecules (2–5 Å), making the van der Waals interaction between pore walls and gas molecules very weak and unfavorable for gas molecule attachment.380 Metalated COFs, however, provide additional opportunities to enhance gas adsorption while retaining the advantages of COFs. Unlike the coordinatively saturated metal ions commonly found in MOFs,395 metal ions in metalated COFs are usually coordinatively unsaturated. These metal ions can induce polarization of gas molecules and promote their adsorption on the open metal sites, thereby providing the possibility for large-capacity gas adsorption under normal temperature and pressure conditions.396
Computational chemistry has played an invaluable role in the studies of gas adsorption of COFs.397–399Ab initio molecular dynamics simulations by Ahuja et al. showed that the hydrogen uptake of the Li(I)-loaded COF-366 at 77 K under ambient pressure is approximately twice that of metal-free COF-366.400 On the basis of the multiscale theoretical method that combines first-principles calculations and grand canonical Monte Carlo simulation, Wang et al. predicted that the total gravimetric hydrogen uptake in COF-202 at 298 K and 100 bar could increase from 1.52 to 3.32 and 4.39 wt% after doping with 3.95 and 7.90 wt% of Li(I), respectively.401 In addition, Li(I)-doping also significantly enhanced the room temperature hydrogen uptake of COF-102, COF-103 COF-105, COF-108, and COF-320.402–405 Furthermore, the diffusion and desorption of hydrogen in COFs were studied by Cheng et al. via combining first-principles calculations and kinetic Monte Carlo simulations. The gravimetric hydrogen density of the Li(I)-doped Pc-PBBA COF was 3.81 wt% at 300 K and 100 bar. When the pressure was reduced to 1 bar, the adsorbed hydrogen molecules showed fast desorption kinetics and 97% of the hydrogen escaped from the material.406 Mechanistically, through charge polarization, the positively charged Li(I) bound to COFs causes the formation of coordination bonds between the electrons of the H2 σ-bonds and the empty Li(I) 2s orbitals, clearly enhancing the hydrogen uptake in the materials.401,402,406 Other alkali and alkaline earth metals, such as Na(I),403 K(I),403 Ca(II),407,408 and Mg(II),407 also enhanced the hydrogen uptake of metalated COFs through similar polarization effects.
Transition metal-chelated COFs also show potential for application in hydrogen storage. For example, according to molecular dynamics simulations using quantum-mechanics-based force fields and grand canonical Monte Carlo simulations, the volumetric hydrogen uptake of PdCl2-chelated COF-301 is 60 g L−1 at 100 bar, which is 8.1 times that of the metal-free COF-301.409 The distance between the adjacent framework layers is reduced from 10.4 to 9.9 Å and the pore size is reduced from 9.3 to 6.3 Å upon PdCl2 loading. The short distance between the metalated sites allows H2 molecules to easily interact with the Pd(II) from the two adjacent layers, and the suitable pore size further enhances this interaction, resulting in the efficient capture of H2. Similarly, simulations by Mendoza-Cortes et al. showed that over a wide pressure range (0–700 bar), the hydrogen uptake of transition metal-metalated imine-COFs was generally higher than that of bulk H2 (Fig. 26).410
 Fig. 26  H2 uptake for metal-free and metalated imine-COFs at 298 K under saturation pressure. (A) Monomers constituting COF-301, COF-322, COF-330, COF-333, COF-340, and COF-350. (B) Optimum pressure, also known as saturation pressure. Under this pressure, the material has the maximum extra uptake relative to bulk H2 at 298 K. (C) Extra gravimetric H2 uptake of pure and metalated COFs at 298 K. (D) Total volumetric H2 uptake of pure and metalated COFs at 298 K. 
In addition to hydrogen adsorption, the enhanced effect of metalation on adsorption of other gases was also investigated by computational chemistry. A simulation study by Smit et al. predicted that the excess CO2 uptake of Li(I)-doped COF-102 was as high as 409 mg g−1 at 298 K and 1 bar, which was 7.9 times greater than that of unmetalated COF-102.411 Similarly, as reported by Wang et al., the excess CH4 uptake of Li(I)-doped COF-103 was 30.98 wt% at 298 K and 35 bar, which was 1.9 times greater than that of unmetalated COF-103.412 Clearly, consistent with hydrogen adsorption, the metalated sites enhance the interaction of gas molecules with the framework, including the London dispersion force and ion-induced dipole interaction, thus significantly increasing their uptake capacity. In addition, Cao et al. investigated the diffusion and separation behaviors of CH4 and H2 in 3D COFs (including COF-102, COF-103, COF-105, and COF-108) and lithium-doped counterparts.413 The affinity of Li(I)-doped 3D COFs for CH4 molecules is stronger than that of H2 molecules, leading to an order of magnitude increase in the adsorption selectivity of Li(I)-doped 3D COFs to the CH4/H2 gas during the adsorption and separation process. However, the self-diffusivity and permeation selectivity of Li(I)-doped 3D COFs were significantly decreased due to the strong affinity of Li(I) for gas molecules, hindering molecular motion. This implies that Li(I)-doping is not favorable for kinetic separation and may weaken the separation performance of COF-based membranes.
The above simulation studies suggest that metalation is a potential method that can enhance gas uptake. However, the simulation results may be difficult to be achieved precisely by chemical methods. For example, the designed COFs may have difficulty in achieving the expected crystallinity or even fail to crystallize, the metal ions embedded in COFs may face difficulties in reaching the theoretical content due to hindered intra-pore mass transfer, the high-valent metal ions may undergo hydrolysis leading to cluster formation, and the open metal ions may coordinate with the solvents leading to coordination saturation, thus weakening the interaction with gas molecules. All these factors lead to gas uptake of metalated COFs to be lower than the calculated value, so that the practical application of metalated COFs in gas adsorption and separation is still limited.
To date, the vast majority of the studies reported in the literature provide the nitrogen adsorption and desorption data of metalated COFs at 77 K.301 However, due to the material weight increase caused by metalation, the gas adsorption per unit weight and specific surface area is usually reduced, indicating that the enhancement of N2 adsorption by metalation is insignificant. However, there are some impressive experimental studies showing the enhanced effect of metalation on hydrogen, carbon dioxide, and ammonia adsorption and release.
In 2020, Johnson et al. reported that the copper(II) formate-loaded COF was heat-treated in vacuum at 175 °C for 1 h to afford open Cu(I) sites in the framework.384 After adsorption of hydrogen, most of the hydrogen was released from the material at 77–173 K. However, a fraction of the hydrogen was retained in the material at room temperature and was not desorbed until 303–373 K. This phenomenon of hydrogen retention at ambient temperature is closely related to the interaction of hydrogen molecules with coordinatively unsaturated Cu(I).
In 2015, Lotsch et al. reported metalation of azine-linked AB-COF by treatment of the COF with lithium acetate and zinc acetate in methanol.414 The metalated Li@AB-COF and Zn@AB-COF displayed enhanced CO2 uptake of 4.33 and 4.68 mmol g−1, respectively, at 273 K and 1 bar, while the CO2 uptake of AB-COF was only 3.38 mmol g−1 under the same conditions. At higher pressure, Li@AB-COF and Zn@AB-COF are more suitable for selective adsorption of CO2 from a mixture of CO2 and H2 than the metal-free AB-COF. By contrast, the metalated ATFG-COF has no beneficial effect on CO2 uptake at 1 bar and in the temperature range of 273–313 K, possibly due to the low amount of open metal sites in ATFG-COF.
Endowing metalated COFs with acidic functionality can significantly enhance NH3 uptake capacity via both the formation of ammonium salts and metal–NH3 interactions. In 2018, Zhu et al. prepared [HOOC]X-COFs (X = 17, 33, 50, 67, 100) containing different amounts of carboxyl groups (Fig. 27A).415 After metalation at room temperature, [MOOC]X-COFs (M = Ca, Mn, Sr; X = 17, 33, 50, 67, 100) were generated (Fig. 27B). Compared with metal-free COFs, the NH3 uptake capacity of [MOOC]17-COF (M = Ca, Mn, Sr) increased from 9.34 to 12.25, 11.38, and 14.30 mmol g−1, respectively. Variable-temperature FT-IR spectra showed that the interaction strength between NH3 and the metal ions decreased in the order of –COOH, –CO, and –NH– in the framework, strongly suggesting that metalation is a key factor for NH3 uptake enhancement (Fig. 27C). A similar phenomenon was observed by Wang et al. in their recent report on the NH3 uptake based on Ca(II)-metalated TAPT-DMTA-COF.416 As shown, the NH3 adsorption of CaCl2@TAPT-DMTA-COF is 8.8 times higher than that of the metal-free TAPT-DMTA-COF. The enhanced NH3 uptake was attributed to the Ca(NH3)xCl2 formation and the capillary condensation phenomenon caused by microporosity.
 Fig. 27  Enhanced NH3 capture performance by introducing acidic groups and open metal sites into COFs. (A) The structure of [HOOC]X-COFs (X = 17, 33, 50, 67, 100). (B) The structure of [MOOC]X-COFs (M = Ca, Mn, Sr; X = 17, 33, 50, 67, 100). (C) The interaction of ammonia and metalated COFs containing carboxyl groups. 
Overall, metalation is one of the effective methods to enhance the gas uptake and selectivity of COFs, which is clearly attributed to the fact that the loaded metal species can provide additional active sites for gas immobilization. Although the metalated COF-based gas adsorption and separation have not been fully explored thus far, the potential of metalated COFs is foreseeable due to the great success of MOFs in gas adsorption and separation.381 We believe that the highly chemically stable frameworks, together with their tunable metal content and metal type, would allow the metalated COFs to be alternative potential porous materials to achieve desirable gas adsorption and separation performance.


3.1.2. Pollutant adsorption. 
In addition to gas adsorption, as porous materials, COFs are also efficient adsorbents for the removal of pollutants, including heavy metal ions,45,417–421 organic dyes,422–426 pesticides,427 and antibiotics.428 In 2019, Tang et al. showed that Ca(II)- and Ni(II)-loaded COF-COOH can facilitate the adsorption-removal of organic dyes.429 A likely explanation for this result is that the loaded metal ions provide increased active sites for dye adsorption, thus improving the efficiency of the organic dye removal. However, frankly, the enhanced effect of metalation on pollutant adsorption has not been fully explored compared to that on gas adsorption.


3.1.3. Enrichment of peptides and proteins. 
Due to the large conjugation range and high density of heteroatoms, COFs have high affinity for peptides and proteins, albeit with poor specificity.430–433 However, metal ions in metalated COFs can provide additional active sites to enhance the selective adsorption of peptides and proteins to a certain extent. In 2019, Lin et al. reported MCNC@COF@Zr(IV) core–shell magnetic nanoparticles, which can serve as an ideal adsorbent for selective enrichment of phosphopeptides via the strong affinity interaction between Zr(IV) and phosphate groups.434 Moreover, the Ti(IV)-anchoring TpPa-2 COF also has a strong affinity for phosphopeptides.435 In mass spectrometric analysis of HeLa cell-derived proteins, 7432 phosphopeptides were detected, showing that the enrichment performance of the Ti(IV)-loaded TpPa-2 COF is superior to that of commercial TiO2 microspheres and the metal-free TpPa-2 COF. Recently, Lin and co-workers reported a Cu(II)-loaded hollow COF that can efficiently capture amyloid β-peptide 1–42, a biomarker of Alzheimer's disease, from human serum within 3 min.436 A low detection limit of 0.2 fmol μL−1 was obtained in the subsequent mass spectrometric analysis.
In addition, metal nanoparticle loaded COFs also possess the ability to selectively enrich polypeptides.318,437 As reported by Li et al. in 2020, IBAs-AuNPs/COF composites with the insulin aptamer on the AuNPs/COF surface exhibit good specificity for insulin enrichment in the presence of high levels of human immunoglobulins, lysozyme, or biotin.335 The selective enrichment of insulin from the serum of diabetic patients by IBAs-AuNPs/COF can then be used for insulin quantification through mass spectrometric analysis.

3.2. Energy storage
In recent years, COFs have been developed as energy storage materials, including in supercapacitors and rechargeable metal ion batteries.438,439 Incorporation of metal ions into COFs would further improve their electrochemical performance and expand the scope of their application.440 Below we will highlight some representative examples in this emerging energy storage area, including semiconductor properties of the metalated COFs and their application in supercapacitors and rechargeable batteries.

3.2.1. Semiconduction and photoconduction. 
As a class of organic materials, COFs are usually electrically insulating, because they share a wide band gap that is too large to allow electrons to transition from the valence band to the conduction band under usual conditions.441 Metalation endows COFs with electrical conductivity in two ways.442 First, the metal acts as an electroactive component to generate charge carriers. Second, the regular arrangement of metal atoms on the COF-scaffolds allows continuous conduction channels for charge transport. Similar to other semiconductor materials, COF-semiconductors can be divided into three types based on their carrier transport characteristics, namely p-type, n-type and ambipolar.443
The stacking of aromatic units in 2D COFs provides a pathway for charge carrier transport. Therefore, p-type semiconducting COFs can be easily constructed by integrating electron-rich units (e.g., porphyrins, phthalocyanines, and pyrenes) into COFs,182,444–446 leading to a carrier transport process dominated by hole conduction. For example, the intrinsic charge carrier mobility of NiPc-COF constructed of nickel(II) phthalocyanine was determined by Jiang et al. using flash-photolysis time-resolved microwave conductivity measurements.53 The charge carrier number was determined to be 3.8 × 108 at a photon density of 6.5 × 1014 photon cm−2 and a bias voltage of 0 V, with a charge carrier generation efficiency of 3.0 × 10−5 that was independent of the measurement atmosphere (i.e., Ar and SF6), indicating its p-type semiconductor behavior with a minimum carrier mobility of 1.3 cm2 (V s)−1. When NiPc-COF was irradiated with a xenon lamp at the wavelengths greater than 400 nm, the current at a bias voltage of 1.0 V increased from 20 nA to 3 μA. Moreover, the Q-band absorption of NiPc-COF was located at 635 and 686 nm, leading to additional sensitivity to dark red light. Additionally, the effect of the central metal on the semiconductor and photoconductive properties was further investigated by comparison of three phthalocyanine-COFs, viz. CuPc-COF, ZnPc-COF, and CoPc-COF.447 The charge carrier mobilities of CuPc-COF, ZnPc-COF, and CoPc-COF at a photon density of 9.1 × 1015 photon cm−2 were 1.4, 2.2, and 2.6 cm2 (V s)−1, respectively. The mobilities increased in the order of CuPc-COF < ZnPc-COF < CoPc-COF, which coincides with the increasing order of electron densities of the phthalocyanine macrocycles, indicating the key role of the central metal in regulating the electronic properties of metallophthalocyanine-COFs. However, the photocurrents of CuPc-COF, ZnPc-COF, and CoPc-COF at a bias voltage of 2 V were 110, 0.6, and 0.14 nA, respectively. This inconsistency with the charge carrier mobility may be related to the microscopic morphology of the three COFs: CuPc-COF is band-like, whereas ZnPc-COF and CoPc-COF are disk-like.
An impressive study by Huang et al. in 2022 showed that piperazine-linked NiPc–NH–CoPcF8 and NiPc–NH–CuPcF8 COFs are p-type semiconducting COFs that exhibit carrier mobilities of 35.4 and 35.1 cm2 (V s)−1 and conductivities of 12.7 and 11.5 S m−1, respectively.219 Remarkably, NiPc–NH–CoPcF8 has the highest carrier mobility among the semiconducting COFs reported to date. In addition to the π-conjugation effect in the metallophthalocyanine-COFs, such record mobility is largely due to the spontaneous oxidation of the piperazine linkages that can lead to the formation of cationic radicals, consequently, increasing electrical performance dramatically.
For exploiting tunable semiconductivity and photoconductivity, Mirica and co-workers constructed a chemiresistive-type gas sensor by using metallophthalocyanine-COF as a semiconductor.215 The aromatic conjugated framework of nickel(II) phthalocyanine-based COF-DC-8 maximizes in-plane charge delocalization, and the regularly arranged rigid metallophthalocyanine entity, together with the fully eclipsed AA-stacking of COF-DC-8, effectively promotes out-of-plane charge transfer. Combining both in-plane and out-of-plane charge transfer strategies, COF-DC-8 has an intrinsic bulk conductivity of up to 2.51 mS m−1. After fabrication into chemiresistive devices, COF-DC-8 exhibited positive chemiresistive response to both NH3 and H2S as electron donors, but negative response to NO and NO2, indicating that COF-DC-8 is a p-type semiconductor. The chemiresistive responses after exposure to gas are linear with respect to gas concentration over a certain range, allowing it to be a gas sensor. The detection limits of NH3, H2S, NO, and NO2 were 0.070, 0.204, 0.005, and 0.016 cm3 m−3, respectively. Importantly, after thermal recovery and solvent treatment, the detection performance of the device is almost restored to its original level, highlighting its reusability. ESR and XPS analysis indicated that weak coordination interactions between gas molecules and Ni(II) were the origin of the chemiresistive response. Similarly, the conductivity of CoPc-PDQ-COF obtained by replacing Ni(II) in COF-DC-8 with Co(II) was measured as 3.68 mS m−1.216
In addition to metallophthalocyanine-COFs, in 2020, Huang et al. synthesized porphyrin-based TAPP-TFPP-COF with tetragonal micropores, in which the porphyrin units form a periodically ordered columnar structure by π-stacking (Fig. 28).194 Due to the lack of charge carriers in the framework, the electrical conductivity of TAPP-TFPP-COF is 1.12 × 10−10 S cm−1 at room temperature, slightly increasing to 6.32 × 10−10 S cm−1 upon visible-light irradiation. After doping with I2, the electrical conductivity of I2@TAPP-TFPP-COF increased to 1.46 × 10−7 S cm−1 due to the formation of charge transfer complexes. Upon visible-light irradiation, the I2@TAPP-TFPP-COF-derived films displayed an increased photocurrent from 22 to 144 nA with a photoconductivity of 4.1 × 10−5 S cm−1. Of note, the I2@TAPP-TFPP-COF films responded to a wide range of wavelengths, and were exceptionally sensitive to 700 nm near-infrared light with an on–off ratio of 24000.
 Fig. 28  Semiconducting iodine-doped porphyrin-based I2@TAPP-TFPP-COF for sensitive near-infrared detection. (A) Spectroscopic detection device based on the TAPP-TFPP-COF film. (B) Response current–voltage curves of TAPP-TFPP-COF and I2@TAPP-TFPP-COF sandwiched between two Au electrodes. (C) Wavelength-dependent on–off switching of photocurrent at 1.0 V. Adapted with permission of ref. 194. Copyright © 2020 American Chemical Society. 
Likewise, the semiconducting nature of porphyrin-based COFs can be used to fabricate gas sensors. In 2022, Lan and co-workers reported that Co-TPCOF prepared by post-synthetic metalation has the form of ultrathin atomic-level thick nanosheets, which is extremely important for providing fully accessible and exposed active sites that facilitate gas diffusion and sensing applications.448 Upon exposure to a NO2 atmosphere, NO2 rapidly adsorbs on cobalt porphyrin to form Co–N bonds and accepts electrons to form nitrite species, leading to an increase in the hole concentration and thus allowing elevated conductivity. Once NO2 is desorbed, electrons are released from the nitrite back to Co-TPCOF and the sensor current is restored. Apparently, metalation enhances the NO2 adsorption on the sensor and contributes to the detection sensitivity. The current response recorded at interdigitated electrodes showed 2713- and 1382-fold current signal enhancement for Co-TPCOF and its unmetalated counterpart H2-TPCOF, respectively, when exposed to 100 cm3 m−3 NO2. Importantly, Co-TPCOF responds selectively to NO2, while 10 other common gases (i.e., SO2, CO, H2S, NH3, CH4, benzene, methylamine, methanol, ethanol, and toluene) do not lead to a change in the current signal. This selectivity is uncommon in chemiresistive-type NO2 sensors and may be related to the significantly lower adsorption energy of NO2 by Co-TPCOF than that of other gases. In addition, the response of Co-TPCOF to NO2 is concentration-dependent with a detection limit of 6.8 × 10−3 cm3 m−3 and a response time of 5.3 min, and the reusability performance and long-term stability meet the needs of practical NO2 gas detection.
Compared with the p-type semiconducting COFs, reports on n-type semiconducting COFs constructed from electron-deficient monomers (e.g. benzothiadiazole and benzobisthiadiazole) are relatively rare thus far.449–451 The first n-type semiconducting COF is the 2D-NiPc-BTDA COF, which was synthesized by Jiang et al. via the reaction of electron-deficient nickel(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine with benzo[c][1,2,5]thiadiazole-4,7-diyldiboronic acid.452 The AA-stacking mode provides a channel for electron transport with an electron mobility as high as 0.6 cm2 (V s)−1. Upon visible-light irradiation, the 2D-NiPc-BTDA COF exhibits panchromatic photoconductivity, and its photocurrent is enhanced from 250 nA to 15 μA.
Very recently, copper(II) phthalocyanine and isoindigo have also been used by the same group to synthesize ordered but unconjugated borate-linked 2D CuPc-MIDA-COF (Fig. 29A).453 The conductivity of CuPc-MIDA-COF is temperature-dependent and can be activated at near room temperature. The activation energy is 0.34 eV and the room temperature conductivity is on the order of 10−6 S cm−1. Based on the Hall effect, the Hall resistance of CuPc-MIDA-COF at 27 °C is linearly and positively correlated with the scanned perpendicular magnetic field, indicating that the charge carriers are electrons with a mobility of 8.3 cm2 (V s)−1. Furthermore, time- and frequency-resolved terahertz spectroscopy indicates that the scattering time of charge carriers is 23 ± 13 fs and the intrinsic carrier mobility is 13.3 cm2 (V s)−1. The structural reasons for such exceptionally fast electron transport were explained based on theoretical calculations. Briefly, in CuPc-MIDA-COF, the electron-deficient monomer isoindigo is guided to form a highly regular overlapping stacking due to the π-stacking of the phthalocyanine species, thereby confining isoindigo to a well-defined framework. Thus, the planar structure allows electrons to move within the plane, leading to lateral electron transport, while the eclipsed stacking enhances electron coupling, permitting band-like electron conduction across the layers (Fig. 29B). This unique electron transport mechanism provides theoretical guidance for the development of high-performance n-type semiconductor materials.
 Fig. 29  (A) Synthesis of CuPc-MIDA-COF using copper(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine and (E)-(1,1′-dimethyl-2,2′-dioxo-[3,3′-biindolinylidene]-6,6′-diyl)diboronic acid. (B) Electron conduction in the CuPc-MIDA-COF framework along the lateral and vertical directions. 
It is clear that the semiconductor properties of metalated COFs are closely related to the type of metal ion. The reaction of (porphyrin-5,10,15,20-tetrayltetrakis(benzene-4,1-diyl))tetraboronic acid and its metalation products with benzene-1,2,4,5-tetraol gave three isostructural porphyrin-COFs with the AA stacking mode (Fig. 30), i.e., H2P-COF, CuP-COF, and ZnP-COF.454 Experimental results showed that H2P-COF is a p-type semiconductor due to the absence of metal and the presence of only ring-to-ring hole transport channels. After doping with metals, additional metal-to-metal electron transport channels are formed. The electron density on the porphyrin rings is reduced in metalated ZnP-COF and CuP-COF, which in turn reduces the ring-mediated hole mobility. However, Cu(II) induces a stronger tendency of ring-to-metal charge transfer than Zn(II), further reducing the electron density on the porphyrin rings, so that CuP-COF is an electron transport-mediated n-type semiconductor, while ZnP-COF allows hole and electron transport along the ring and metal, respectively, as an ambipolar semiconductor. This pioneering study by Jiang and co-workers implied that by changing the metal species in metalated COFs, not only the conductivity can be fine-tuned, but also the carrier type can be fundamentally changed.
 Fig. 30  p-Type, n-type, and ambipolar semiconducting porphyrin-COFs. (A) The structures of MP-COFs (M = H2, Cu, Zn). (B) Schematic diagram of ring-to-ring and metal-to-metal channels for hole and electron transport, respectively. 
The combination of electron-rich donors and electron-deficient acceptors in COFs can form ambipolar semiconducting COFs.455–457 Jiang et al. reported the synthesis of DZnPc–ANDI-COFs (Fig. 31A) from zinc(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine as the electron donor and ((1,3,6,8-tetraoxo-1,3,6,8-tetrahydrobenzo[lmn][3,8]phenanthroline-2,7-diyl)bis(4,1-phenylene))diboronic acid as the electron acceptor, in which the acceptor and donor form parallel columnar arrays that allow ultrafast electron transfer from donor to acceptor, enabling direct coupling of light absorption and charge separation and suppressing charge recombination.458 Both solid-state and multiple organic solvent-dispersed DZnPc–ANDI-COF can produce photo-induced rapid charge dissociation and long-life charge retention. Further studies of photo-induced electron-transfer dynamics have shown that the photo-induced charge separation state lifetime and charge carrier mobility are influenced by factors such as metal type and the donor–acceptor distance.209
 Fig. 31  Donor–acceptor COFs. (A) DZnPc–ANDI-COF constructed from electron-donating and electron-accepting monomers. (B) [C60]y–ZnPc-COF composed of the electron donor on the framework and the electron acceptor in the pore. 
In addition to the use of different monomers, regularly arranged donor and acceptor in COFs can be constructed by the pore engineering strategy. According to the research of Jiang et al., x%N3–ZnPc-COFs (x = 0, 10, 25, 50) with azide groups on the pore walls were synthesized using zinc(II) 2,3,9,10,16,17,23,24-octahydroxyphthalocyanine as the node and different ratios of (2,5-bis(azidomethyl)-1,4-phenylene)diboronic acid and 1,4-phenylenediboronic acid as the edge.459 Photoelectroactive [C60]y–ZnPc-COFs (y = 0.3, 0.4, 0.5) were obtained after click reactions with fullerenes modified with ethynyls (Fig. 31B), in which the fullerenes are confined in the pores as electron acceptors and the phthalocyanines on the frameworks act as electron donors, leading to photoinduced electron transfer and allowing effective charge separation in the form of spatially separated ZnPc˙+ and C60˙−. As a result, upon laser flash at 680 nm, [C60]0.3–ZnPc-COF exhibited a charge separation time of 2.66 ms. This work demonstrates the possibility of using frameworks and regular pores to construct ambipolar COFs for charge separation and photoelectric conversion, highlighting the advantages of COFs over amorphous polymers.
In conclusion, COFs can be used as semiconductors and photoconductors due to the π-column periodic arrays resulting from their stacked structure,460 while metal ions can modulate the photoelectric activity of COFs by adjusting the local electron density, providing a valuable toolbox for property optimization.


3.2.2. Supercapacitor. 
According to their electrical energy storage mechanisms, supercapacitors—also called electrochemical capacitors—are classified as either pseudocapacitors, electrochemical double-layer capacitors, or hybrid supercapacitors.461 Pseudocapacitors, also known as redox supercapacitors, are based on the electrochemical adsorption of ions on the surface of electrode materials and subsequent reversible redox reactions. The introduction of variable-valent metals (e.g., Ni, Co, and Fe) and redox-active monomers (e.g., quinone, imide, and thianthrene) into COFs may help to achieve pseudocapacitance.462–464 Electrochemical double-layer capacitors store electric energy through charge accumulation at the electrode–electrolyte interface without chemical reactions.465 As porous materials, COFs have a high specific surface area for providing ample charge storage surface and suitable pore size (1–4 nm) for the transport of solvated ions within the pores, which may help to improve the energy density of electrochemical double-layer capacitors.466
The earliest COF device capable of pseudocapacitive energy storage was constructed using 2,6-diaminoanthraquinone as the redox active site.467,468 However, it is difficult to precisely control the number of active sites in order to fine-tune the electrochemical performance. In 2015, Jiang et al. used post-synthetic modification of nickel(II) porphyrin-COFs to covalently attach 2,2,6,6-tetramethylpiperidine-1-oxyl (TEMPO) to the framework of [HCC]X%-NiP-COF (X = 50, 100) in order to convert the COFs into a redox-active platform for capacitive energy storage (Fig. 32).135 The resulting [TEMPO]X%-NiP-COFs (X = 50, 100) have capacitances of 124 F g−1 (X = 50) and 167 F g−1 (X = 100) at a current density of 100 mA g−1. This study underscored that the regular pores of COFs promote charge transfer, and the high specific surface area provides a platform for the immobilization of redox-active sites, revealing the potential of COFs as an important platform for the construction of energy storage materials.
 Fig. 32  Redox-active radical [TEMPO]50%-NiP-COF for pseudocapacitive energy storage. 
In 2021, Zhang and co-workers reported dioxin-linked metallophthalocyanine-derived PAE-PcM (M = Co, Ni, Cu) COFs as p-type semiconductors for supercapacitors.469 The effects of different metals in COFs on the properties were compared. Since the carrier mobility increases in the order of PAE-PcCu < PAE-PcNi < PAE-PcCo, PAE-PcCo with the best semiconductor performance was used to develop supercapacitors. Structurally, PAE-PcCo can accommodate large electrolyte ions due to its open pore channel with a diameter of 1.4 nm. Experiments using a three-electrode system in 0.5 M 1-ethyl-3-methyl-1H-imidazol-3-ium chloride showed the capacitance characteristics of PAE-PcCo in a wide potential window with a range of −0.6–0.8 V. The surface area-normalized capacitance of PAE-PcCo devices is 19 μF cm−2, and the devices retain 86% of the capacitance after 1500 cycles at 80 mV s−1. Mechanistically, the capacitance of PAE-PcCo is mainly attributed to the redox process during charge–discharge cycles with a maximum contribution of 88.5% and a relatively small contribution from the double-layer capacitance. In addition, the solid-state supercapacitor cell has a low internal resistance with an equivalent ohmic resistance of only 2.2 Ω. Clearly, the excellent stability of the dioxin-linked COFs paves the way for the application of COF-based devices.
COFs have also recently been developed as electrochemical double layer capacitors. In 2020, Fang et al. reported that amino-functionalized metalloporphyrins, i.e., 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin nickel(II) and copper(II), reacted with 4,4′-(ethyne-1,2-diyl)bis(2-hydroxybenzaldehyde) to result in JUC-511 and JUC-512, respectively.470 Structurally, both COFs have open pores with a size of 3.4 nm that are conducive to charge transfer. Due to the existence of hydrogen bonds between –OH and imine linkages, the chemical stability of JUC-511 and JUC-512 is greatly improved. The areal capacitance values of the capacitor device manufactured based on exfoliated JUC-511 and JUC-512 at 1000 mV s−1 are 5.46 and 5.85 mF cm−2, respectively. After 10000 cycles, the capacitance retention rates are still close to 100%, indicating their good reliability and stability. In addition, considering the low density of COFs, exfoliated JUC-511 and JUC-512 capacitors with the maximum power densities of 55.0 and 42.2 kW kg−1, respectively, are superior to the common graphite carbon microcapacitors for achieving device miniaturization. It is particularly important to mention that even at a scan rate as high as 30000 mV s−1, the device still shows excellent energy storage performance, which is not common in capacitor-type microdevices. By contrast, the metal-free JUC-510 was also synthesized from 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin, and it showed electrochemical properties inferior to those of JUC-511 and JUC-512, suggesting that metalation can indeed improve the capacitor performance.
Hybrid supercapacitors based on metalated COFs were reported recently. In 2020, Zhuang et al. reported the interdigital microsupercapacitors that were assembled from the metallophthalocyanine-based PAE-NiNiPcF8 COF and exfoliated graphene (Fig. 33).214 The highly ordered crystalline framework and periodically arranged metal-on-metal columns in the PAE-NiNiPcF8 COF provide powerful transport channels for charge carriers. The specific volumetric capacitance of the PAE-NiNiPcF8 COF device reaches 28.1 F cm−3 at a scan rate of 2 mV s−1. In an acidic electrolyte, the PAE-NiNiPcF8 electrode exhibits outstanding cycling stability. The capacitance performance is over 98% of the initial value after 10000 charge–discharge cycles. Trasatti analysis suggests that the contributions of pseudocapacitance and double layer capacitance behavior are approximately equal for the PAE-NiNiPcF8 COF-derived device. In addition, PAE-CuCuPcF8 and PAE-NiCuPcF8 based devices with different metal centers display slightly lower capacitive performances, with specific volumetric capacitances of 22.0 and 24.1 F cm−3 at a scan rate of 2 mV s−1, respectively.
 Fig. 33  Metallophthalocyanine-COFs as hybrid supercapacitors for energy storage. (A) Structure of PAE-NiNiPcF8, PAE-CuCuPcF8, and PAE-NiCuPcF8 COFs with dioxin linkages. (B) Cyclic voltammetry curves at a scan rate of 50 mV s−1 with approximately rectangular shape. (C) Specific volumetric capacitances at the scan rates ranging from 2 to 50 mV s−1. (D) Galvanostatic charge–discharge curves at a current density of 0.04 mA cm−2. Adapted from ref. 214 under the terms of the Creative Commons CC BY license. Copyright © 2021 The Authors. Published by Wiley-VCH GmbH. 


3.2.3. Rechargeable battery. 
Conventional organic electrode materials usually suffer from poor electrical conductivity, slow ion diffusion, low energy density, and poor cycling stability.471 Inspired by redox-active COFs and their potential as supercapacitor energy storage devices, the prospect of redox-active COFs in metal-ion battery systems has also attracted significant attention.472 First, COFs have regular open pores with easily functionalized pore walls. The modified functional groups on the pore wall can interact with metal ions to modulate ion transport, thus inducing uniform and dense metal deposition during charge and discharge, and ultimately suppressing dendrite growth. This is critical for increasing battery capacity and extending battery life.438 Second, the diversity of building blocks and topologies enables COFs with tunable structures to facilitate functional-oriented material design.473 The customizability of COFs provides outstanding flexibility in the optimization of the battery performance. Ion diffusion kinetics and conductivity of a COF-based battery can be optimized by exfoliating bulk COFs362,474,475 and compounding with other conductive materials, such as carbon nanotubes.476–478 Third, COFs have lower material density and higher energy density compared to MOFs and other metal-based materials.479 Also, the good thermostability and electrochemical stability of COFs undoubtedly can extend the cycle life of batteries.480 To date, COFs have already been used to make lithium-ion,481–483 sodium-ion,484–486 potassium-ion,487,488 zinc-ion,489,490 lithium–CO2,491 lithium–sulfur,492–494 and zinc–air batteries.221 Functionally, COFs can be used as anodes,362,475,495 cathodes,478,496,497 solid-state electrolytes,498–500 and separators.501–505
As we know, the regularly arranged metal-on-metal arrays are favorable for charge carrier transport, and the variable-valence metals can be used as redox-active sites, as evidenced by several recently reported examples.
In 2021, Lan et al. reported the application of a manganese(II) porphyrin-COF in Li–CO2 batteries.201 As shown in Fig. 34A, TTCOF-Mn was synthesized as a cathode catalyst for high-performance nonprotonic Li–CO2 batteries by imine condensation between electron-donating 4,4′,4′′,4′′′-([2,2′-bi(1,3-dithiolylidene)]-4,4′,5,5′-tetrayl)tetrabenzaldehyde and catalytically active manganese(II) 5,10,15,20-tetrakis(4-aminophenyl)porphyrin monomers. TTCOF-Mn exhibited higher CO2 uptake than its metal-free counterpart TTCOF-2H (29.8 vs. 14.0 cm3 g−1). When used as a Li–CO2 battery cathode, the overpotential of TTCOF-Mn is only 1.07 V at a high current density of 100 mA g−1, which is less than half of that of TTCOF-2H. Importantly, the Li–CO2 battery with TTCOF-Mn as the cathode can operate at a high current density of 300 mA g−1 for 180 cycles, with only a slight decrease in the discharge terminal potential from the initial 2.86 V to 2.60 V, while TTCOF-2H shows a rapid decrease in the discharge terminal potential to 1.60 V after 10 cycles (Fig. 34B). In the deep charge–discharge experiments, the discharge capacity of TTCOF-Mn is 13018 mA h g−1, which is 3.1 times higher than that of TTCOF-2H. On the one hand, the mechanistic study shows that the metalloporphyrin in TTCOF-Mn as the catalytically active center in the Li–CO2 battery effectively adsorbs and activates CO2 to realize an efficient four-electron CO2 conversion pathway; on the other hand, the electron-donating property of tetrathiafulvalene and the regular microporous channel are favorable for the transport of electrons and Li(I) ions. This study suggests a positive role of metalation in improving the performance of COF-electrodes.
 Fig. 34  Li–CO2 battery cathode catalysts based on metalated COFs. (A) Structure of manganese(II) porphyrin-based TTCOF-Mn with a single Mn(II) metal site and multifunctional transfer channel. (B) Battery life cycles of TTCOF-Mn and TTCOF-2H cathode catalysts at a current density of 300 mA g−1. Adapted with permission of ref. 201. Copyright © 2020 The Authors. Published by American Chemical Society. (C) Chemically exfoliated MnO2/DQTP-COF-NS-3 as a cathode catalyst in Li–CO2 batteries. (D) Discharge–charge cycling curves of MnO2/DQTP-COF-NS-3 with a limited capacity of 1000 mA h g−1 at a current density of 200 mA g−1. (E) Long-term cycling curve of the MnO2/DQTP-COF-NS-3 cathode catalyst at a current density of 1.0 A g−1. Adapted from ref. 327 under the terms of the Creative Commons CC BY-NC-ND 4.0 license. Copyright © 2021 The Authors. Published by Elsevier Inc. 
Loh et al. established the ternary composite, which is composed of COF-Ru@CNT formed by the acylhydrazone-linked Tf-DHzOPr COF, ruthenium nanoparticles, and carbon nanotubes, for use as a cathode in a Li–CO2 battery.506 The Tf-DHzOPr COF provides regular pores to promote CO2 adsorption and Li(I) directional transport, and ruthenium nanoparticles contribute to CO2 reduction and Li2CO3 decomposition. The synergy between Tf-DHzOPr COF and ruthenium catalyst effectively reduces the accumulation of Li2CO3 on the cathode and avoids passivation of the cathode surface and blockage of diffusion channels, thus narrowing the overpotential and enhancing the battery kinetics. This enables the battery to run for many cycles and withstand high current densities. The data show that for the Li–CO2 battery, the overpotential of the COF-Ru@CNT cathode is only 1.24 V. The battery has an ultra-large capacity of 27348 mA h g−1 at a current density of 200 mA g−1, and is cycled through 200 charge–discharge cycles without a significant performance decay under a current density of 1000 mA g−1.
Exfoliation of bulk COFs into nanosheets can further expose the active sites. Very recently, the same group reported that the Mn-involved MnO2/DQTP-COF-NS-3 nanosheet can be achieved by the reaction of DQTP-COF and HClO4-acidified KMnO4 solution with 18.9 wt% MnO2 (Fig. 34C).327 MnO2/DQTP-COF-NS-3 nanosheets with the MnO2 catalyst and the redox-active anthracene-9,10-dione moiety would be of great benefit for the mass transfer and battery kinetics. As expected, MnO2/DQTP-COF-NS-3 displays excellent electrochemical performance as a cathode catalyst for Li–CO2 batteries, exhibiting a discharge potential of 2.72 V and a charge potential of 4.18 V at a constant current density of 200 mA g−1 and a limited capacity of 1000 mA h g−1 (Fig. 34D). The specific capacity reaches an astonishing 42802 mA h g−1 based on the full discharge curves at a current density of 200 mA g−1. Furthermore, the Li–CO2 battery can be rapidly charged and discharged at a high current density of 1000 mA g−1 for 120 cycles without significant performance degradation (Fig. 34E).
In addition to Li–CO2 batteries, the application of metalated COFs in other types of batteries has also been reported by Wang and co-workers.362 E-TFPB-COF/MnO2 composite nanosheets prepared by a similar chemical stripping method were used as anode materials for lithium-ion batteries. The E-TFPB-COF/MnO2 composite anode has long cycling stability with a high reversible capacity of 1359 mA h g−1 at a current density of 100 mA g−1 after 300 cycles, whereas this reversible capacity is 968, 126, and 358 mA h g−1 for E-TFPB-COF nanosheets, bulk TFPB-COF, and commercial MnO2, respectively. There are many reasons for this result. First, the broad conjugation range of E-TFPB-COF promotes Li(I)–π interactions, providing outstanding lithium storage performance. Second, compared to bulk TFPB-COF, the ultra-thin micromorphology exposes more redox-active sites. Third, the short insertion distance of Li(I) substantially promotes their diffusion. Lastly, acting as a spacer, MnO2 nanoparticles prevent the agglomeration of E-TFPB-COF nanosheets during the cycling charging and discharging process.
Exploiting the coordination interaction between cyano and Co(II) in COF-316, Wang and co-workers realized its metalation.507 The obtained COF-316-Co was used as the anode for potassium-ion batteries. Due to the K(I)–π interactions and structural defects caused by Co(II), COF-316-Co has stronger conductivity and faster K(I) reaction kinetics than COF-316. The charge transfer resistance of the COF-316-Co anode is significantly lower than that of the COF-316 anode. The reversible capacity was 371 mA h g−1 after 400 cycles at 100 mA g−1, which is 3.5 times higher than that of COF-316 (106 mA h g−1).
In 2021, the same group reported a zinc–air flow battery, in which the aqueous solution of ferric phthalocyanine-based COFBTC, KOH (8 M) and ZnO (0.5 M) served as the electrolyte, and the zinc plate and IrO2/C on carbon paper acted as the anode and air cathode, respectively.221 Unlike the conventional air cathode that is coated with the catalyst (e.g., Pt/C), the COFBTC solution catalyst allows the active sites to be almost completely exposed, which is clearly beneficial for improving battery performance. For the discharge process, COFBTC has good activity with an onset potential of 965 mV and a half-wave potential of 900 mV. After 10000 cyclic voltammetry cycles, the half-wave potential shifted by only 9 mV. Furthermore, at a current density of 10 mA cm−2, the COFBTC-constructed battery maintains its properties for 40 discharge–charge cycles, while its counterpart constructed using Pt/C as the catalyst exhibits significant performance degradation after 10 cycles.
Unarguably, metalated COFs have made some progress in battery applications due to the availability of a catalytic active center and ion diffusion channels, but there are still a lot of research gaps, providing great opportunities for future studies. The electrode reactions which will be discussed in the next section may provide additional information for increasing energy density and optimizing battery performance.

3.3. Electrocatalysis
Noble metal-catalysts, such as Pt, RuO2, and IrO2, as electrocatalysts have been widely investigated for use in electrolytic cells, fuel cells, and metal–air cells.508,509 However, the poor stability and high cost of precious metal electrodes have greatly limited their performance and large-scale applications.510 The development of next-generation electrocatalysts with enhanced stability and catalytic activity is an ongoing challenge in energy conversion and storage research.511,512 Electrocatalysts based on metal-free materials and inexpensive metals such as graphene,513,514 MXenes,515,516 MOFs,517–520 and COFs126,479 are currently an active research area. Due to the well-defined and programmable structures, the study of COF-electrocatalysts can truly correlate the structure and properties and promote a deeper understanding of electrocatalytic principles, thus providing guidance for the development and optimization of novel electrocatalysts.438,521,522 Compared to conventional metal-based materials, COFs have relatively less active sites and lower conductivity, making the direct application of most pristine COFs in electrocatalysis difficult. Methods such as introduction of heteroatoms,523,524 metalation,134,300,525 defect engineering,526 and preparation of composites527,528 are usually utilized to introduce catalytic active sites and further enhance the electrochemical properties of COFs. In particular, metalated COFs combine the advantages of COFs and metal-based materials, offering an alternative platform for the integration of conductivity, porosity, and catalytic activity into a single scaffold.

3.3.1. Electrochemical water splitting. 
Electrochemical water splitting, involving hydrogen evolution reaction (HER) at the cathode and oxygen evolution reaction (OER) at the anode, is considered an attractive approach for the sustainable production of clean and renewable energy.510
In principle, HER, the process by which H+ or H2O receives electrons to be reduced to hydrogen gas, occurs through the Volmer–Heyrovsky–Tafel mechanism that involves three main reactions, namely initial electron transfer (Volmer step), electrochemical desorption (Heyrovsky step), and composite desorption (Tafel step). The reaction kinetics of the Volmer step are fast, and either the Heyrovsky step or the Tafel step is usually the rate-determining step of HER. As an example of HER application of metalated COFs, Feng et al. explored the HER performance of cobalt porphyrin-based Co-2DP deposited on a Ti electrode in a KOH solution.139 The electrode overpotential was 367 mV with a Tafel slope of 126 mV dec−1 at a current density of 1.0 mA cm−2 due to the CoN4 active site. Furthermore, rhenium-metalated COF-Re designed by Marinescu et al. catalyzes HER with a faradaic efficiency of 11% in 0.5 M KHCO3 solution at a potential of −1.1 V.227 After introducing Co(II) and Fe(II) into the porphyrin moiety of COF-Re, the faradaic efficiencies were increased to 55% and 65%, respectively. Moreover, in 2022, Chen et al. reported Ru(III)-metalated COF-1 as an efficient electrocatalyst for HER in 0.5 M H2SO4.529 Due to the protonation of the triazine ring, it has a Tafel slope of 140 mV dec−1 and an overpotential of 200 mV at a current density of 10 mA cm−2.
OER is a four-electron process in which water is oxidized to oxygen. Due to the high energy barrier of O–H bond breaking and OO bond formation, the actual potential of OER is higher than the theoretical value (1.23 V).511 Therefore, OER is generally considered to be the rate-limiting step in electrochemical water splitting.
The Co(II)-metalated TpBpy COF was one of the first metalated COFs investigated for OER, as reported by Kurungot et al.136 Co-TpBpy-coated glassy carbon electrodes in 0.1 M phosphate buffer at pH = 7 required an overpotential of 400 mV to generate an anodic current density of 1.0 mA cm−2. The Tafel slope was 59 mV dec−1. The performance remained stable in 1000 cycle scans and 24 h activity tests. Furthermore, using polystyrene as a hard template, the introduction of interconnected macropores into the Co-TpBpy COF can facilitate the mass transfer process and enhance the accessibility of the active species, further improving the OER performance.235 The Tafel slope of Co-TpBpy with macropores was 54 mV dec−1, and the overpotentials were 380 and 430 mV at current densities of 10 and 50 mV cm−2, respectively.
In addition, in 2021, Chen et al. prepared Co@COF-Pyr and Ni@COF-Pyr catalysts for OER under alkaline conditions with pyrimidine as the binding site for metal ions.530 The Tafel slopes of Co@COF-Pyr and Ni@COF-Pyr are 100 and 145 mV dec−1, respectively, which are both significantly lower than that of their metal-free counterpart COF-Pyr (879 mV dec−1). Similarly, the COF-TpDb-TZ-Co formed by the coordination of tetrazole-functionalized COF-TpDb-TZ with Co(II) is an OER catalyst under alkaline conditions, with a Tafel slope of 82 mV dec−1, which is much lower than that of COF-TpDb-TZ (477 mV dec−1).531
The synergistic effect of Ni(II) and other metal ions can optimize the OER kinetics.525 For example, the Tafel slope of the heterobimetallic NiFe-Salphen-COF is 53 mV dec−1, which is lower than that of Ni-Salphen-COF (72 eV dec−1).300 The OER performance of IISERP-COF2 deposited with different ratios of Co(OH)2 and Ni(OH)2 in 0.1 M KOH depends on the Ni:Co mass ratio.527 The best OER performance was obtained for the Ni:Co mass ratio of 3:1, with an overpotential of 258 mV and a Tafel slope of 38.9 mV at a current density of 10 mA cm−2.
Recently, Deng et al. used machine learning to predict the performances of metalated 3D salen-COFs in OER and identified Ni-salen-COFs to be the best candidate.532 The synthetic experiments well verified the predicted results, and the Ni-salen-COF was overall better than the corresponding Co-, Fe-, Cu-, and Zn-based analogs in Tafel slope, charge transfer resistance, and electrochemical double-layer capacitance. This theoretical and experimental study not only develops the synthesis method of metalated COF electrocatalysts, but also provides insights for material design.
Several strategies may help to further enhance the OER properties of metalated COFs, including the use of monomers with OER activity to construct COFs533 and the preparation of composites with carbon nanomaterials to enhance electrical conductivity.528 Although these strategies have been confirmed to be effective for other types of materials, they have not been extended to metalated COFs.


3.3.2. Electrocatalytic oxygen reduction. 
Oxygen reduction reaction (ORR) is a key electrode reaction in fuel cells and metal–air batteries.534 Although the detailed mechanism of ORR is not fully understood, it can be simply divided into a four-electron pathway and a two-electron pathway.535 In the four-electron pathway, O2 is reduced to H2O and OH− in acidic and alkaline media, respectively.536 In the two-electron pathway, O2 is reduced to either H2O2 (in acidic media) or HO2− (in basic media). Subsequently, H2O2 or HO2− can either diffuse into solution or can be further reduced to H2O or OH−.537
Benefiting from tunable structures, large specific surface areas, and well-defined nanoscale pores, heteroatom-involved COFs have been explored as ORR electrocatalysts, but their performance is constrained by the limited active site density and poor conductivity.538 Metalation of COFs is demonstrated to be an effective approach to access COF-based ORR electrocatalysts with rich and precisely controlled electrocatalytically active sites.
Metal–N4 catalytic centers in metalloporphyrin-COFs are considered to be potential alternatives to noble metal ORR catalysts. On the basis of first-principles calculations, Xia et al. identified the crystal field stabilization energy of metals as an activity descriptor to predict the ORR performance of metalloporphyrin-COFs and predicted that iron(II) and cobalt Co(II) porphyrin-based COFs may be a superior catalyst for four-electron ORR.539 The experimental results obtained by Wu et al. were consistent with this prediction.540 Co-, Mn-, and Ni-metalated porphyrin-COFs, termed as M-TP-COF (M = Co, Mn, Ni), were prepared by [4+4] imine condensation. For M-TP-COF (M = Co, Mn, Ni), the onset potentials were 0.81, 0.75, and 0.72 V, respectively; the half-wave potentials were 0.73, 0.68, and 0.66 V, respectively; and the diffusion-limited current densities were 4.8, 5.0, and 2.2 mA cm−2, respectively. These data indicated that Co-TP-COF has better ORR performance than Mn-TP-COF and Ni-TP-COF. In addition, the electron transfer number of Co-TP-COF during ORR was determined to be 3.7, indicating that Co-TP-COF mainly catalyzed four-electron ORR in alkaline electrolytes.
It is clear that in addition to metal ions, the structure of COFs can also affect the ORR mechanism and therefore it is difficult to generalize the above trends to all imine-linked COFs. In 2020, Chen et al. systematically investigated the effect of metal ions in the imine-linked metalloporphyrin-COFs on the catalytic activity of ORR (Fig. 35).541 According to the disk current density and disk onset potential results obtained for the three oxygen-saturated electrolytes at pH of 12.6, 7.2, and 3.5, among the seven metalated COFs, COF-366-Fe had the highest ORR activity, followed by COF-366-Ni and COF-366-Mn. However, the three COFs with the highest selectivity for H2O2 generation were COF-366-Co, COF-366-Ni, and COF-366-Ir, as reflected by their electron transfer number and faradaic efficiency values. Among these, COF-366-Co had 91% H2O2 selectivity and 84% faradaic efficiency in oxygen-saturated 0.1 M KOH, exhibiting high selectivity toward H2O2 generation via the two-electron ORR. Furthermore, the H2O2 productivity of COF-366-Co in an H-shaped electrolyzer was as high as 909 mmol (g h)−1 at a current density of 22 mA cm−2. This study demonstrates that metalated COF-catalyzed two-electron ORR is an attractive approach for decentralizing H2O2 production, providing a powerful complementary technique to the anthraquinone process used in industrial production of H2O2.
 Fig. 35  Electrocatalytic ORR performance of metalloporphyrin-based COF-366-M (M = Mn, Fe, Co, Ni, Cu, Zn, Ir). (A) Structure of COF-366-M. (B) Structure of metal-free COF-366-2H. (C) Disk current density at the overpotential of 0.1 V vs. RHE (RHE, reversible hydrogen electrode). (D) Onset potentials for the disk electrode. (E) Ring current intensity at the overpotential of 0.1 V vs. RHE. (F) Onset potentials for the ring electrode. (G) The proportion of O2 reduced to H2O2, defined as H2O2 efficiency. (H) ORR electron transfer number. (I) Faradaic efficiency. 
The fabrication of metal nanoparticle-loaded COFs has proved to be a feasible strategy for enhancing ORR performance by improving the electronic properties. The Pt@TM-TPT-COF electrocatalyst, with a Pt content of 6.4 wt%, was obtained by Jiang et al. via loading nanoplatinum in fully conjugated TM-TPT-COF.356 In 0.1 M HClO4 saturated with O2, Pt@TM-TPT-COF displayed an onset potential of 1.04 V and a half-wave potential of 0.89 V, which were 0.07 and 0.06 V lower than those of commercial Pt/C, respectively. The electron transfer number of Pt@TM-TPT-COF in ORR is 3.9–4 in the potential range of 0.2–0.8 V, indicating that Pt@COF mainly carried out four-electron ORR in acidic electrolytes. In addition, due to the immobilization of Pt by triazine N on the TM-TPT-COF scaffold and the high chemical stability of the TM-TPT-COF matrix, the current density of Pt@TM-TPT-COF retained 96% of the initial value after running for 50 h, highlighting the excellent stability of Pt@TM-TPT-COF.
Phthalocyanine-based CoPc-dx-COF catalyzed four-electron ORR in 0.1 M KOH, but its high resistance limits its performance.213 Simple mixing of CoPc-dx-COF with carbon materials improved ORR performance by increasing the conductivity. Moreover, high-temperature carbonization of metalated COFs is also a useful strategy for enhancing electrical conductivity and ORR activity.229,234,526,542


3.3.3. Electrocatalytic CO2 reduction. 
Sustainable energy demands and global climate change have spurred the development of methods to convert CO2 into value-added carbon products, motivating the broad research interest in the electrochemical CO2 reduction reaction (CO2RR).543 CO2RR is a highly complex multi-proton and multi-electron transfer reaction with many reaction intermediates.544 The variety of possible CO2RR products—such as C1 compounds (e.g., CO, CH4, HCOOH, and CH3OH) and C2 compounds (e.g., acetic acid, ethylene, and ethane)—makes selectivity a formidable challenge.545 Furthermore, because most CO2RR reduction potentials are close to that of HER, HER is usually a competing side reaction that needs to be avoided as well.46,546
The application of metalated COFs in CO2RR began with the study of the electrocatalytic activity of cobalt porphyrin-COFs by Chang et al.134 Cobalt porphyrin-based COF-366-Co (Fig. 36A and B), as the first reported CO2RR COF-electrocatalyst, reduced CO2 to CO in NaHCO3 solution at an overpotential of −0.55 V with a faradaic efficiency of 90%. In a diaphragm electrolytic cell, COF-366-Co as the cathode coating material was maintained for at least 24 h with a total CO production of 36 mL mg−1. After the electrocatalytic reaction, the crystallinity and microscopic morphology of the recovered COF-366-Co were not significantly changed, allowing reuse for 5 times without decreasing the catalytic activity and selectivity. Although the electrocatalytic performance of the investigated COFs was comparatively poor, this landmark work highlights the high potential of metalated COFs as electrocatalysts for CO2RR.
 Fig. 36  Cobalt porphyrin-based COFs for CO2RR under alkaline conditions. (A) Schematic diagram of the diaphragm electrolytic cell. (B) Structure of COF-366-Co. (C) Strategies to regulate the CO2RR activity of cobalt porphyrin-based COFs. 
In the follow-up study, a series of strategies were adopted to improve the CO2RR activity and selectivity of Co-metalated COFs (Fig. 36C). COF-367-Co with a larger pore size than that of COF-366-Co showed enhanced catalytic CO2RR activity, possibly due to adequate active site exposure.134 At an overpotential of −0.55 V, the 24 h CO production corresponding to COF-367-Co was 2.8 times higher than that of COF-366-Co, exceeding 100 mL mg−1, while the CO faradaic efficiency was comparable to that of COF-366-Co. In addition, the structural flexibility of metalated COFs provides an opportunity to fine-tune the active centers. Replacing the cobalt porphyrin in COF-367-Co with copper porphyrin with no CO2RR catalytic activity dilutes the active CoN4 sites, further improving the accessibility of the active site and enhancing the CO2RR activity, but decreasing the selectivity for CO2 reduction.134
The charge transport within the COF-layer allows electronic connectivity between remote functional groups and active sites, thus enabling precise regulation of CO2RR catalytic activity. Cobalt porphyrin-COFs modified with electron-withdrawing groups on the pore walls were reported by Yaghi et al. in 2018.547 The current density at a given electrolytic potential increases in the order of COF-366-Co, COF-366-(OMe)2-Co, and COF-366-F4-Co, which is consistent with the order of the intensity of the electron-absorbing effects observed by X-ray absorption spectroscopy. The CO2RR performance of COF-366-F4-Co is slightly decreased due to strong hydrophobicity, which is not consistent with the above-described observed trend.
The introduction of electron donors into porphyrin-COFs can enhance the conductivity and improve the electrocatalytic CO2RR activity. TTF-Por(Co)-COF containing tetrathiafulvalene has higher conductivity and carrier mobility than COF-366-Co; this is ascribed to the existence of efficient electron transfer from the tetrathiafulvalene scaffold to the cobalt porphyrin moiety.548 Electrochemical tests showed that the current density and the faradaic efficiency of TTF-Por(Co)-COF were higher than those of COF-366-Co over the tested potential range. For example, at an applied potential of −0.7 V, the faradaic efficiency of CO2 to CO conversion of TTF-Por(Co)-COF reached 95%, significantly higher than that of COF-366-Co (70.8%). Furthermore, on the basis of the same strategy, Cao et al. reported the installation of thieno[3,2-b]thiophene into the framework of a cobalt porphyrin-based COF to enhance the CO2RR activity.196 However, excessive electron transfer may lead to the hydrogenation of porphyrin N that degrades the long-term durability performance of the catalyst, which must be considered. Interestingly, crown ethers not only enhance electron transfer but also improve the hydrophilicity and CO2 adsorption of COFs. TAPP(Co)-B18C6-COF with 18-crown-6 as a scaffold, reported by Liu et al. in 2021, is an excellent candidate for the CO2RR catalyst with a maximum turnover frequency of 1267 h−1 at −0.9 V and a maximum CO faradaic efficiency of 93.3% at −0.7 V.549
The construction of 3D COFs is another effective approach to enhance the activity of CO2RR. The 3D COFs reduced the porphyrin stacking and allowed the electrocatalytic sites to be exposed to the electrolyte and CO2 as much as possible, thereby enhancing the catalytic activity. The 3D-Por(Co/H)-COF synthesized by Cao et al. in 2022 with a Co content of 0.56 wt% achieved a high faradaic efficiency of CO up to 92.4% at −0.6 V in 0.5 M KHCO3.550 Its electrocatalytic activity was higher than that of COF-366-Co and other previously reported 2D porphyrin-COFs.
Growing porphyrin-COFs on the surface of conductive scaffolds can further optimize CO2RR performance. Zhu et al. synthesized COF-366-(OMe)2-Co@CNT using aminated carbon nanotubes as a template, in which the COF-366-(OMe)2-Co nanolayer grown on the carbon nanotube scaffold was only 0.9 nm thick, increasing the accessibility of the Co(II) active sites and conductivity.551 In CO2-saturated KHCO3, COF-366-(OMe)2-Co@CNT exhibited high selectivity for the reduction of CO2 to CO, with a faradaic efficiency of 93.6% at −0.68 V and a current density of up to 40 mA cm−2 at −1.05 V, both of which are much higher than those of its counterparts without carbon nanotubes. Not surprisingly, although the thick COF-366-(OMe)2-Co coating increases the number of Co(II) active sites, it also blocks the electron transport channel from the carbon nanotubes to Co(II), weakening the synergistic effect and thus is detrimental to CO2RR.
In addition to cobalt porphyrin, cobalt phthalocyanine, which also has CoN4 active sites, is also an effective molecular catalyst for CO2RR.552,553 Since 2020, several examples of 2D cobalt phthalocyanine-COFs for CO2RR have been reported.147,212,216,220 In these COFs, the metallophthalocyanines are connected by strong covalent bonds, including phenazine, imide, and dioxin linkages, to form robust planar sql lattices. On the one hand, electrons can be transported in the planes through the highly conductive regular lattices. On the other hand, the metal-on-metal columns formed by metallophthalocyanine stacking promotes electron transport in the direction perpendicular to the 2D layer. Therefore, these COFs have high CO2RR activity and CO selectivity (Table 5). For example, as reported by Jiang et al., CoPc–PI-COF-1 provided large CO partial current densities of 21.2 mA cm−2 at −0.90 V and 9.4 mA cm−2 at −0.7 V, associated with its high conductivity of 3.72 × 10−3 S m−1. CoPc–PI-COF-1 was stable for 40 h in an electrocatalytic test at −0.70 V, showing no performance decay with a turnover number (TON) as high as 277000.220 It is important to mention the contribution of irreversible chemical bonds in dioxin-linked COFs to the durability of the CO2RR.147,212 The CoPc–TFPN COF was stable for 60 h at −0.9 V and the faradaic efficiency of CO was maintained at 94.5–97%.212 In addition, nickel phthalocyanine-based NiPc-COF was also used for CO2RR, showing a CO faradaic efficiency of approximately 96% and a turnover frequency (TOF) of 1.05 s−1.218
