(B) Inhibitory effect of Fe-iCOF and GFeF on S. aureus in the presence or absence of glucose. (C) Wound healing promoted by GFeF in mice infected with S. aureus. Adapted with permission of ref. 150. Copyright © 2021 Wiley-VCH GmbH. 
Nanosilver is a traditional broad-spectrum antimicrobial metal material. In 2022, Dong et al. obtained Ag@DhaTph-COOH by loading silver nanoparticles in a porphyrin-based DhaTph-COOH COF (Fig. 61).319 Ag@DhaTph-COOH has photothermal and photodynamic properties that can be combined with nanosilver to enhance the antimicrobial effect. The inactivation efficiency of Ag@DhaTph-COOH exceeded 95% for bacteria (including E. coli and S. aureus) and viruses (including influenza A virus subtype H1N1 and vesicular stomatitis virus) under a laboratory xenon lamp and even real sunlight. In addition, hydroxyl-rich Ag@DhaTph-COOH was cross-linked with isocyanate-terminated polyurethane oligomers, and after it was sprayed onto the surface of nonwoven polyester fabric, a bioprotective mask with a self-sterilized surface was obtained. Bacteria and viruses attached to the mask were inactivated within 60 min under sunlight exposure. The contaminated mask was regenerated by washing with water and ethanol, with no apparent performance loss after 5 repeated uses.
 Fig. 61  Nanosilver-loaded DhaTph-COOH COF as the self-sterilized coating of bioprotective mask against bacteria and viruses. Adapted with permission of ref. 319. Copyright © 2022 The Royal Society of Chemistry. 

4. Summary and outlook
Although COFs have the advantages of customizability, high stability, and colourful reaction chemistry and have a wide range of applications, they have some inherent limitations in their properties and applications as pure organic materials.128 The morphology control and processability of COFs are difficult due to the low density, large internal space, and interlayer molecular interactions that are much weaker than covalent bonds. For example, the synthesized COF-based membrane is loose and fragile and has poor reusability.861 Furthermore, the synthesis of nanoscale COF particles necessitates an inefficient exfoliation strategy.119,806 In addition, the poor hydrophilicity of COFs increases the mass transfer resistance in aqueous systems, which is limited in sensing, catalysis, and biomedical applications. More critically, the function of COFs is confined to the limited properties caused by the monomers and their stacking, disregarding more than 4/5 of the metal elements in the periodic table. In contrast, the application-oriented porous materials used in gas adsorption and separation,862,863 catalysis,520,864,865 electrochemistry,866 and biomedicine867,868 heavily rely on the properties endowed by metals rather than the organic moieties. In this context, metalated COFs offer an opportunity to balance the structural advantages and functional limitations of COFs, with impeccable porosity, crystallinity, stability, functionality, and tunability. After more than 10 years of development, metalated COFs stand at the intersection of inorganic chemistry and organic chemistry. They are organic–inorganic hybrid materials, much like MOFs, which have been widely developed and have numerous application prospects. However, the development of metalated COFs is still in the stage of raw material collection and faces some systemic challenges.
The coordination chemical environment of the metal unquestionably influences the material properties in metalated COFs. Several issues should be considered when synthesizing metalated COFs. Are there multiple metal ion binding sites in the framework? What is their contribution to the immobilized metal ions? Do metals form clusters through metal–metal and metal–heteroatom bonds? In addition to the framework, what are the other molecules that form coordination bonds with metals? What additional role dos the ubiquitous defects in COFs play in binding metal ions? The answers to these questions will deepen the understanding of the structure–property relationships and may enable function-oriented material design. Furthermore, it is important to note that current characterization techniques are incapable of unambiguously determining the chemical purity, stacking pattern, crystal domain size, defect density, and many other structural features of COFs.86,869–872 Each of these features with uncertainties may impact the interaction of metal ions with COFs, which further complicates the structure–property relationships of metalated COFs.
Theoretical calculations are powerful tools for studying the structure and properties of materials; for example, first-principles calculations, molecular dynamics simulations, and grand canonical Monte Carlo simulations have been applied in the study of the binding sites of light metals in COFs,402 optimization of the unit cell structure of COFs,852 prediction of gas adsorption behaviors,412,873,874 and design and screening of electrocatalysts.532,875,876 However, due to computational bottlenecks, theoretical simulations are usually performed on fragments of COFs, leading to one-sided conclusions. Moreover, even such degraded theoretical calculations are rarely used to optimize the metalation synthesis conditions, catalyst screening, prediction of electronic properties, and material–biointerface interaction studies, although they are logically feasible and very important.
Artificial intelligence is changing research paradigms in various disciplines, including chemistry and materials science, with the ability to predict and discover unknown information by learning from existing datasets.877 Artificial intelligence bypasses the concrete understanding of structure–property relationships, providing a black-box tool for discovering new structures, new properties, and new applications.878–881 Because the COF structure is highly predictable, a database of COF structures has been established based on combinations of known and predicted building blocks. It contains more than 470000 hypothetical materials.99 In addition, a database of real structures based on published data was also initially established.882 These provide training sets for high-throughput screening and machine learning. Adding the metal dimensionality to these established datasets enables the construction of datasets for the study of metalated COFs. There are, however, two main challenges. First, as mentioned above, the binding sites of metal ions in metalated COFs have not been completely identified, which reduces the accuracy of the dataset and thus increases the training and predictive difficulties of machine learning. Second, the COF structure report lacks a unified standard, and the establishment of the dataset has to rely on manual extraction of structural information from the literature and manual proofreading.873,874,882 We strongly recommend that the community unifies the structure reporting standard of COFs and provides machine-readable standardized format files, which can greatly promote the application of data science in exploring the potential of COFs. We believe that it is only a matter of time before artificial intelligence reshapes the study of metalated COFs.
In conclusion, the library of metal ions and organic monomers with suitable coordination sites for the synthesis of metalated COFs is growing as the research proceeds. The field of metalated COFs will continue to be an active and challenging area of research. We hope that this review article will inspire follow-up studies on metalated COFs and even functionalized COFs.

Table Content:

Qun Guan
	Qun Guan is currently a PhD student. He received his bachelor's degree in chemistry from the University of Jinan in 2015. He received his master's degree in organic chemistry from Shandong Normal University under the guidance of Prof. Yu-Bin Dong in 2019 and has subsequently continued his PhD studies. His research focuses on nanoscale COFs for cancer diagnosis and therapeutics.

Le-Le Zhou
	Le-Le Zhou received her master's degree in organic chemistry from Shandong Normal University under the supervision of Prof. Yu-Bin Dong in 2018. Then, she worked as a lecturer at the School of Chemical and Biological Engineering, Qilu Institute of Technology, from 2018 to 2020. Currently, she is a PhD student under the supervision of Prof. Yu-Bin Dong. Her research interests are advanced materials for preventing and treating tumors.

Yu-Bin Dong
	Prof. Dr Yu-Bin Dong is the Chang Jiang Scholar of chemistry at Shandong Normal University. He obtained his PhD from Nankai University (under Prof. Li-Cheng Song) in 1996. He then joined Prof. Andreas Mayr's group at The University of Hong Kong and Prof. Hans-Conrad zur Loye's group at the University of South Carolina from 1996 to 2000, and was promoted to full professor at Shandong Normal University in 2000. He is the author of over 200 peer-reviewed publications. His current research interests are mainly focused on MOF and COF materials and their applications in catalysis, sensing, bioimaging, and cancer treatment.
